```markdown
A PLUME BOOK

戰爭、和平與戰爭

PETER TURCHIN 是康涅狄格大學生態學和革命生物學系教授。他是技術著作《歷史動力》的作者，其中他呈現了《戰爭、和平與戰爭》所發展出的宏觀理論背後的統計數據。

“許多關於各種歷史事件的迷人討論，以清晰、生動的文筆呈現。這本書的結果，與 Jared Diamond 的《槍、疾病和鋼鐵》有許多相似之處，是對世界歷史的一項刺激性的修正主義概述。”

—Publishers Weekly

“這是一個關於世界歷史的迷人理論，值得專業人士和大眾認可。它既具有挑戰性又令人愉悅閱讀。”

—Paul Seabright, 來自圖爾索大學（University of Toulouse）的作者，《陌生人的公司：經濟生活的自然史》，The Company of Strangers: A Natural History of Economic Life

“當托馬斯·霍布斯在十七世紀提出他的國家理論時，他提出了關於政治的‘理性科學’的案例， variously 被認為是荒謬、褻瀆、 cynical、醜陋，或者只是不切實際。但他們無法做的事情之一就是忽視霍布斯。Peter Turchin 對帝國歷史的解釋可能會引起爭議，但它也無法被忽視。他的理論既耀眼又具有挑戰性，值得歷史學家辯論、分析和質疑。這是一個極具時效性的提醒，即歷史並非僅僅是一篇敘述，而是一個隨著其自身的原則和邏輯展開的過程。”

—Philip Ball, 《臨界質量：一件事引發另一件事》的作者，Critical Mass: How One Thing Leads to Another

“Turchin [是] 當代演化理論中的領先人物…… 他現在將這些見解應用於人類歷史…… 他以俄羅斯帝國 fortune 的波動為人所知，這與 contemporaneous 紀錄中關於莫斯科和克里米亞、俄人和圖們人的關係以及他詳細描述的關係有關。他從其基礎分析中提取了這個長期存在的歷史例子與新美國人在不斷變化的邊疆上擴張的相似之處。本書的大部分內容都專注於對羅馬帝國崛起及其隨後衰落的一項案例研究，這又以精簡和華麗的方式進行，時間跨度為一個千年。 《戰爭、和平與戰爭》旨在面向最廣泛的讀者群體，並以敘述性的方式解釋一切。Turchin 的文筆非常引人入勝。”

—Gordon Johnson,劍橋大學 Wolfson College 院長，在《泰晤士高等教育雜誌》（Times Higher Education Supplement）上
```

Section path: Document

“這裡科學家圖欽……面對歷史的顯而易見的混亂性，並通過數學模型和行為理論的棱鏡得出結論，認為存在持久的循環式歷史模式，他稱之為克洛迪動力學……在許多方面，圖欽對世界歷史的看法與傑拉德·戴姆斯的觀點相衝突，正如他在《槍、病菌與冰戶》一書中所表達的。他的假設預示著會引起爭議。”

—Library Journal

序言

“和平帶來戰爭，戰爭帶來和平”

帝國終於統一了所有文明。經過數代的戰鬥之後，最後的敵人都被擊敗了。帝國的公民似乎可以期待永久的和平與繁榮。但是，一位名叫哈里·塞爾頓的異端數學家給出了令人不安的消息。他新興的精神物理學科學，建立在整合無數個個體行為的方程式之上，預測了大規模社會趨勢。當這些方程式向前運行時，它們預言了中央權力的衰落和最終崩潰、各個地區公爵和將軍的反叛，以及最後一場苦難的內戰，將帝國的首都從數十億人潮擁擠的繁榮都市變成幾千名掙扎求生的幸存者的鬼城。這位謙遜數學家所說的事情，正在按照他的預言展開。

└── 《文件》

├── 第一章：宇宙與歷史
│   └── 亞瑟·C·史域的預言學
│       └── 預言學是“處理人類群體對固定社會和經濟刺激反應的數學分支”
│       └── 預言學的準確性並非絕對。預言學無法準確地預測單個人的行為。此外，預言的知識必須從被預測者的群體中隱藏。
│       └── 預言人類社會可能會變得不可能，因為複雜的動態系統在長遠來看是不可預測的，因為“蝴蝶效應”。小的原因可能產生巨大的影響。例如，澳大利亞的一隻無地蝶的翅膀拍打可能會導致大西洋上的颶風。或者，正如兒童詩歌所說，“因為缺少一根釘子……國王失了。”
│       └── 儘管阿西莫夫三部曲吸引了數百萬讀者的想像力，其中包括許多科學家和歷史學家。然而，他的願景與大多數專業歷史學家和科學家的觀點相悖，這種觀點在我們文化中被廣泛接受。
│

```markdown
Section path: Document

A science of history sounds cold and hard—wouldn’t it destroy our enjoyment of the wonderfully rich tapestry of the past? 在歷史學的觀點來看，顯得冰冷而刻板——這 wouldn't it 摧毀我們對過去那種豐富多彩的圖案的享受？

On a darker side, might not such a science enable some shadowy cabal to manipulate societies to a nefarious purpose? 而且，這種學科是否能使一些陰影中的勢力操縱社會以達到邪惡的目的？

But have we ceased to enjoy the blue sky of a brilliant summer day, or the play of colors in a glorious sunset? 但我們是否已經停止欣賞明媚夏日藍天，或在壯麗的日落中欣賞色彩的變化？

After all, the physicists, beginning with Newton and ending with Einstein, worked out exactly how colors of the sky result from the interaction of sunlight with the atmosphere. 畢竟，從牛頓到愛因斯坦開始並結束的物理學家們已經確切地闡述了天空顏色是如何通過陽光與大氣層相互作用而產生的。

As to the nefarious uses of a science of history, it is true that any knowledge can be turned to good or bad ends. 關於歷史學的邪惡用途，確實是說任何知識都可能被用於善或惡的目的。

But Asimov’s notion of a Second Foundation—a group of psychohistorians pulling the strings from some secret center—was always the least credible part of his vision. 但阿西莫夫對“第二基礎”——一群從某個秘密中心拉動琴弦的心理歷史學家們的想法，一直是他的願景中最不可信的部分。

War and Peace and War addresses the question raised by Asimov (and many other people before him, including Marx and Tolstoy): Is a science of history possible? 《戰爭與和平》探討了阿西莫夫（以及在他之前許多人，包括馬克思和托爾斯泰）提出的問題：歷史學是否可能？

Can we design a theory for the collapse of mighty empires that would be no worse than, say, our understanding of why earthquakes happen? 我們能否設計一種解釋強大帝國崩潰的理論，而且這個理論不會比我們對地震發生的原因理解差多少？

Seismologists have made great strides in understanding earthquakes. They can even make some limited predictions as to which areas of the earth are likely to be hit next by an earthquake. 地震學家在了解地震方面取得了很大進展。他們甚至可以對哪些地區最有可能受到地震襲擊做出一些有限的預測。

However, forecasting the precise timing and magnitude of an earthquake eludes them. 然而，準確預測地震的時間和規模仍然逃不過他們的魔爪。

Can a science of history, similarly, explain why states crumble, and perhaps predict which societies are in the danger of collapse? 歷史學是否也能夠像這樣，解釋國家為何崩潰，並可能預測哪些社會面臨崩潰的危險？

THIS BOOK FOCUSES ON EMPIRES. 這本書專注於帝國。

Why did some—initially small and insignificant—nations go on to build mighty empires, whereas other nations failed to do so? 一些——最初很小且不重要的——國家是如何發展成強大的帝國，而另一些國家卻未能做到這一點的？

And why do the successful empire builders invariably, given enough time, lose their empires? 並且，成功的帝國建設者不可避免地，在足夠的時間內失去他們的帝國嗎？

Can we understand how imperial powers rise and why they fall? 我們能否理解帝國勢力如何崛起以及它們為何衰落？

An empire is a large, multiethnic territorial state with a complex power structure. 帝國是一個擁有複雜權力結構的大型、多民族的領土國家。

The key variable is the size. 關鍵變數是規模。

When large enough, states invariably encompass ethnically diverse people; this makes them into multiethnic states. 當足夠大時，國家不可避免地包含來自不同族群的人；這使它們成為多民族國家。

And given the difficulties of communication in pre-industrial times, large states had to come up with a variety of ad hoc ways to bind far-flung territories to the center. 並且，在工業時代之前，由於溝通的困難，大型國家不得不想出各種臨時解決方案來將遙遠的地區與中心聯繫起來。

One of the typical expedients was to incorporate smaller neighbors as self-contained units, imposing tribute on them and taking over their foreign relations, but otherwise leaving their internal functioning alone. 其中一種常見的手段是將較小的鄰國納入自為運作的單位，對其徵稅並接管其外交關係，但除此之外，仍然讓它們的內部運作不受干擾。

Such a process of piecemeal accumulation usually leads to complicated chains of command and the coexistence of heterogeneous territories within one state. 這種零散積累的過程通常導致複雜的指揮系統和同一國家的內部分別存在多樣化領域共存。
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

Empires 並非一學科研究的唯一對象。歷史學家如阿諾·代爾比（Arnold Toynbee）撰寫了大量關於整個文明興衰的研究著作。其他人則對世界宗教的傳播、藝術風格的演變、科學技術的進步，或經濟和人口方面的變化而著迷。所有這些主題都值得研究。然而，不可能將它們全部納入一本書之中。 帝國的興衰是一個好的起點。

與如文明般的實體不同，領土國家更容易定義和界定彼此之間的差異，以及與其他可比單位（如城邦、部落聯盟等）的差異。歷史學家們仍在爭論如何區分一個文明與另一個文明。不同的權威機構將阿契美尼德帝國歸類為西諾亞、伊朗或美索不達米아文明之一。相反，如果您諮詢任何歷史地圖集，您會發現阿契美尼德帝國的邊界幾乎在同一地點繪製。

儘管帝國的活動主導了歷史記錄，但我們不應得出它們是人類歷史中的常規這一結論。在19世紀之前，地球上大部分可居住空間（以及6000年前所有人）都由小型、非國家社會瓜分，而非帝國。歷史上的帝國本身，經常處於衰退或解體的狀態。一個內部穩定且和平的大型帝國在歷史上是罕見的。從這個角度來看，最基本需要解釋的問題並不是為什麼帝國衰落和崩潰，而是他們是如何開始運作的？ 帝國如何可能存在？

帝國的故事引人入勝。想像一下18世紀英國人的感受，在他們環球旅行中，站在保存良好的2000年前的古羅馬廢墟之中（在現代都市吞噬它們之前）。今天，您可以在墨西哥的奇琴伊察也能有類似的體驗。（請務必提早一天早上到達，在遊覽巴士到達之前。）這些人們是誰建造了這些宏偉的神廟和金字塔？ 他們現在不在我們這裡了，原因是什麼？ 從雪萊的《奧西曼迪亞》到達斯·維德，帝國的故事總是吸引著我們。

作為對接下來內容的路線圖，以下是一個非常簡潔的書中主要理論論證大綱。

許多歷史過程是動態的——帝國興衰、人口和經濟繁榮和衰退、世界宗教傳播或凋零。 歷史動力學這個領域研究這些動態過程在歷史中的表現。 大部分研究都集中在農業社會上，即大多數（以及經常超過90％的人口）參與食物生產的社會上。
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

The theoretical framework I have been developing for several years focuses not on human individuals, but on social groups through time。最終，一個群體的行為是由其個體成員的行動所決定的。然而，社會群體並非簡單的相同粒子集合，容易用統計物理學描述；它們具有複雜的內部結構。

一個重要的群體結構方面是不同的人擁有不同的權力和財富。在農業社會中，少數成員（通常約 1 或 2 ％）集中了大多數權力和財富；這一群體由精英或貴族組成。平民則構成剩餘的人口。

另一個重要的社會結構方面是民族。民族是指任何文化面向的群體使用方式，以創造內部凝聚力和與其他群體的區別。一種虛構的界線將民族群體的成員與人類的其他部分隔離開來。例如，希臘人劃分了自己與異族、非希臘語使用者之間的界限。民族界限可以使用各種象徵標誌——語言和方言、宗教和儀式行為、種族、服裝、行為舉止、髮型、飾品和紋身。重要的是哪些標誌被使用，而關鍵在於在內群體與外群體之間，以及“我們”與“他們”之間的區分。

人們通常具有多重民族身份，這些身份相互嵌套。達拉斯的一名居民可以同時是德克薩斯人、美國人，也是西方文明的參與者。通常將 объединяющих многие страны наиболее широкие группы людей称为文明，但我更喜欢将这些实体称为元民族社群（来自希腊语“meta”，意为“超越”和“ethnos”，意为“民族”或“国家”）。我的定義不僅包括典型的文明——西方、伊斯蘭和漢族——還包括如凱爾特人和圖赤摩爾人等廣泛的文化群體。通常，不同元民族社群的人之間存在最大的文化差異；有時這種差距非常極端，以至於人們否認那些在元民族斷層線的另一側的人的全部人性。

歷史動力可以理解為由群體之間的競爭和衝突所導致的結果，其中一些群體控制著另一些群體。然而，這種控制只有因為群體在微觀層面上通過成員之間的合作而整合才得以實現。內群體合作是跨群體衝突的基礎，包括其極端形式，如戰爭甚至大屠殺。
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

不同群體之間成員的合作程度各不相同，因此具有不同的凝聚力和團結性。 依照第十四世紀阿拉伯思想家伊本·哈倫（Ibn Khaldun）的觀點，我將這種群體的特性稱為「阿斯比雅」（asabiya）。 阿斯比雅指的是社會群體進行協調集體行動的能力。 阿斯比雅是一種動態量數；它會隨著時間而增加或減少。 就像牛頓物理學中的力量等許多理論建構物一樣，協調集體行動的效能無法直接觀察到，但可以從可觀測到的後果中衡量。

每個帝國的核心都是皇室民族。（有些帝國在某一段時間內擁有多個皇室民族，但這種結構似乎不穩定。） 帝國擴張領土和抵禦外部及內部敵人的能力很大程度上取決於其皇室民族的特性，尤其是其阿斯比雅。 因為只有具備高水平阿斯比雅的群體才能構建大型帝國，所以問題是他們如何獲得它，以及最終他們為什麼會失去它？

具有高阿斯比雅的群體產生於跨族裔邊境。 跨族裔邊境是指皇室界限與兩個跨族裔社群之間的分歧線重疊的區域。 跨族裔邊境是兩者群體之間競爭非常激烈的場所。 擴張主義帝國對其領外的人民施加巨大的軍事壓力。 然而，邊境人口也受到帝國財富的吸引，他們試圖通過貿易或襲擊來獲得這些財富。 外在威脅和獲利前景都是培養阿斯比雅的強大整合力量。 在跨族裔邊境這種高壓環境下，未能充分融入的群體會瓦解消失，而以強烈合作為基礎的群體則蓬勃發展並擴張。

為了與舊帝國匹敵，具有高阿斯比雅——一種萌芽期的皇室民族——的邊境群體需要通過吸收其他群體來擴張。 在跨族裔邊境上，同一側分歧線上的同族群體由於存在截然不同的「異類」——位於另一側的跨族裔社群而更容易融入。 跨越邊境的巨大文化差異遠大於同一側族群之間相對較小的差異。 實證證據表明，在政治界限將文化上相似的人民分隔開的地方，不會出現大型侵略性帝國。

因此，我的主要論點是，起源於分歧線邊境的人們會被培養出合作精神和高水平的協調集體行動能力，從而使他們能夠構建大型而強大的領土國家。 我在第一部分闡述這個論點，並用俄羅斯和美國（第 1 章和第 2 章）、羅馬邊境上的德意志人和阿拉伯人（第 3 章和第 4 章）、羅馬的起源（第 6 章）以及歐洲大國崛起（第 7 章）的例子加以說明。
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

The critical assumption in my argument is that cooperation provides the basis for imperial power. This assumption is at odds with the fundamental postulates of the dominant theories in social and biological sciences: the rational choice in economics and the selfish gene in evolutionary biology. However, recent developments in the nascent fields of experimental economics and multilevel selection show that the standard model, based on the self-interest hypothesis, is deeply flawed. It cannot explain the puzzle of human ultrasociality—our ability to combine into cooperating groups consisting of millions of unrelated individuals. Moreover, it is refuted by behavioral experiments.

Two key adaptations enabled the evolution of ultrasociality. The first one was the moralist strategy: cooperate when enough members in the group are also cooperating and punish those who do not cooperate. A band that had enough moralists to tip its collective behavior to the cooperative equilibrium outcompeted, or even exterminated, bands that failed to cooperate. The second adaptation, the human ability to use symbolic markers to define cooperating groups, allowed evolution of sociality to break through the limits of face-to-face interaction. The scale of human societies increased in a series of leaps, from the village and clan to the tribe and tribal confederation, and then to the state, empire, and civilization. Chapter 5 examines this new science of cooperation.

WHEREAS PART I IS DEVOTED TO IMPERIOGENESIS—the factors that explain the rise of empires—Part II switches focus to imperiopathosis—why empires decline.

The very stability and internal peace that strong empires impose contain within them the seeds of future chaos. Stability and internal peace bring prosperity, and prosperity causes population increase. Demographic growth leads to overpopulation, overpopulation causes lower wages, higher land rents, and falling per capita incomes for the commoners. At first, low wages and high rents bring unparalleled wealth to the upper classes, but as their numbers and appetites grow, they also begin to suffer from falling incomes. Declining standards of life breed discontent and strife. The elites turn to the state for employment and additional income, and drive up its expenditures at the same time that the tax revenues decline because of the growing misery of the population. When the state’s finances collapse, it loses the control of the army and police. Freed from all restraints, strife among the elites escalates into civil war, while the discontent among the poor explodes into popular rebellions.
```

```markdown
## 文件路徑：Document

The collapse of order brings in its wake the four horsemen of the apocalypse—famine, war, pestilence, and death. Population declines and wages increase, while rents decrease. As incomes of commoners recover, the fortunes of the upper classes hit bottom. Economic distress of the elites and lack of effective government feed the continuing internecine wars. However, civil wars thin the ranks of the elites. Some die in factional fighting, others succumb to feuds with neighbors, and many simply stop trying to maintain their aristocratic status and quietly slip into the ranks of commoners. Intra-elite competition subsides, allowing the restoration of order. Stability and internal peace bring prosperity, and another cycle begins. As a sixteenth-century commentator put it, “So peace brings warre and warre brings peace.”

The typical period of a complete cycle, which consists of a benign integrative phase and the troubled disintegrative phase, is around two or three centuries. I call these majestic oscillations in demographic, economic, and social structures of agrarian societies secular cycles. The demographic-structural theory that explains secular cycles is developed in Chapters 8 and 9, in which it is illustrated with French and English history during the medieval and early modern times.

The phase of a secular cycle affects a trend in economic and social inequality, which in turn affects the dynamics of asabiya. Incipient imperial nations are relatively egalitarian. Great differences in wealth among group members undermine cooperation, and such groups succumb to rivals with higher levels of asabiya. In addition, metaethnic frontiers tend to be underpopulated, so there is enough land (the main form of wealth in agrarian societies) for all who are willing to work it. The success of an imperial nation at territorial expansion, however, results in the movement of frontiers far away from its core, thus removing an important force holding up the growth of inequality Imposition of peace results in population growth, and overpopulation brings with it the impoverishment of peasant masses. As the poor grow poorer, the rich grow richer—this process is called the Matthew principle. The growing disparity between the rich and the poor puts the social consensus under strain. At the same time, the gap in the distribution of wealth grows not only between the aristocrats and commoners, but also within each social group. Intra-elite competition for diminishing resources results in faction and undermines national solidarity. During the disintegrative phase of the secular cycle, regional and sectarian identities acquire greater saliency than the national or empire-wide identity, and the asabiya of the imperial nation is corroded. Thus, the Matthew principle plays an important role in imperiopathosis, the decline of empires.
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

Decline of asabiya is not linearly uniform. During the integrative phases of secular cycles when inequality is moderate, intra-elite competition and conflict between elites and commoners subside; the empire-wide identity regains its strength, for a time. As discussed further in Chapter 10, it takes the cumulative effect of several disintegrative phases to reduce asabiya of a great imperial nation to the point where it cannot hold together its empire.

A life cycle of a typical imperial nation extends over the course of two, three, or even four secular cycles. Every time the empire enters a disintegrative secular phase, the asabiya of its core nation is significantly degraded. Thus, several secular cycles are nested within the great cycle of the rise and decline of asabiya. However, disintegrative phases are also not uniformly grim. A civil war begins like a forest fire or an epidemic—violence leads to more violence in an escalating spiral of murder and revenge. Eventually, however, people become fed up with constant fighting, and a civil war “burns out.” Both the survivors of the civil war and their children, who had direct experience of conflict, are reluctant to allow the hostilities to escalate again. They are, thus, “immunized” against internecine violence. The next generation, the grandchildren of the civil warriors who did not experience its horrors at first hand, is not immunized. If the social conditions leading to conflict (the main one being elite overproduction) are still operational, the grandchildren will fight another civil war. As a result, civil war tends to recur during the disintegrative phase with a period of 40 to 60 years. I call such dynamics the fathers-and-sons cycles. The fathers-and-sons cycles are nested within secular cycles, which in turn are nested within asabiya cycles. I illustrate these “wheels within wheels within wheels” dynamics with the decline of the Roman Empire in Chapter 11.

In this book, therefore, I discuss three central concepts: the metaethnic frontier theory, which explains asabiya cycles; the demographic-structural theory, which explains secular cycles; and the social-psychology theory, which explains the fathers-and-sons cycles. These theories comprise part of a new science of historical dynamics, or as I prefer to call it cliodynamics (from Clio, “muse of history,” and dynamics, “the study of processes that change with time”).
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

Cliodynamics 借鑒了自然科學領域的兩個學科。關注群體而非個人，與統計力學的方法相似，統計力學通過對無數粒子運動的積分來預測群體的性質，例如溫度或壓力。然而，研究和預測人類群體是一個更具挑戰性的任務，因為人們在（包括權力和民族認同在內）諸多方面存在差異。人類也具有自由意志。我在第 12 章中討論了這些複雜因素對人類社會的研究影響。

Cliodynamics 更進一步地借鑒了非線性動力學的學科。人類社會和國家可以被建模為動態系統，由相互作用的部分組成。此外，國家是國際體系的一部分，這增加了額外的複雜性。這裡的核心概念是動態反饋。一個系統的組件狀態變化會影響另一個組件，但後者可能會反向影響（反饋）前者。當一個動態系統包含循環非線性反饋時，它會變得非常容易產生振盪。簡而言之，“和平帶來戰爭，而戰爭也帶來和平”。

然而，歷史社會和國家的週期並不是像物理學中行星運動或擺動的這種高度周期性、可重複的現象。社會系統遠比這複雜得多。非線性動力學科學表明，兩個或多個完全周期的行為疊加在一起可能會產生非周期的動力學——也就是混沌。阿莎比亞、世俗和父子關係週期之間的相互作用可能導致這種複雜的混沌動力學。在一個混沌系統中，其一個元素的（人類行爲自由意志）小動作可能會產生巨大的後果。外部來源也發揮作用——例如，氣候變化導致作物歉收、隨機突變導致新的可怕疫情以及火山爆發等。由於混沌行為、自由意志和自然災害的性質，真實的人類社會無法在遠未來準確預測，因此哈里·塞爾頓是錯的。
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

Although prediction far in the future is impossible, given what we know about societies and nonlinear dynamics, it does not mean that improved understanding of how societies function is purely academic knowledge. An understanding of the processes that bring a society to the brink of civil war might suggest policies to avert such a war. Such social engineering, of course, is still far in the future. Our understanding of the dynamics of even agrarian societies is far from perfect, and highly complex modern industrial and postindustrial societies present an even greater challenge for sociologists. Many processes that played a determining role in the functioning of agrarian societies are of much less or even no importance in modern societies. For example, famine has been largely eliminated in modern Western societies. On the other hand, human nature has not been completely changed by the Industrial Revolution. In the last two chapters of this book, I speculate on what lessons cliodynamics might have for us and our future times of war and peace and war.

第一部分

帝國起源

帝國崛起

第一章

一群冒險家擊敗了一個王國

伊馬克的征服柯薩克人

1581年10月22日，戰士伊馬克·季米提耶夫（一位領導數百名柯薩克人的阿塔曼）決定在伊рты什河畔紮營。柯薩克人在烏拉爾山遠處的敵對領土中，各方面都受到野蠻勢力的包圍。夜已經降臨，他們點燃了一圈篝火以防禦潛伏襲擊並保暖傷員。在紮營後，伊馬克召集了未受傷者和不守衛的人們討論下一步該怎麼做。他們選擇不多，而且都不令人滿意。

Part I

IMPERIOGENESIS

The Rise of Empires

Chapter 1

A Band of Adventurers Defeats a Kingdom

Ermak’s Conquering Cossacks

On October 22, 1581, the warrior Ermak Timofeev, an ataman leading several hundred Cossacks, decided to make camp on the banks of the Irtysh River. The Cossacks were deep in the hostile territory on the far side of the Urals, surrounded by savage hordes on every side. Night had already fallen, so they lit a ring of fires to guard themselves against stealthy attack and to keep warm their wounded comrades. After making camp, Ermak gathered together the unwounded and those not keeping watch to discuss what they must do next. They had few options, and none looked good.
```

```markdown
## 文檔路徑：Document

鏈條導致這些俄羅斯戰士來到伊рты什的事件，始於數十年前，於 1558 年，沙皇伊凡四世授予雅各布和格里戈里·斯特羅甘諾夫在烏拉爾山脈西部的荒野上卡馬地區一個巨大的領土。 斯特羅甘諾夫家族是荷蘭人和英國商人探險家和帝國建設者的對應人，他們在東方和西印度群島創立了貿易公司。 在十六世紀早期，斯特羅甘諾夫家族在俄羅斯東北邊的邊疆地區發展了大規模工業——鹽提取、皮毛貿易和漁業，因此他們有經驗和資本來開發新的領土。 斯特羅甘諾夫兄弟立即吸引移民並建立定居點和軍事據點。 這片土地由各種芬諾烏戈爾民族的原住民稀少地居住著，儘管他們對入侵感到怨恨，但無法提供有效的抵抗。 更嚴重的威脅來自居住在烏拉爾山脈以外的草原和森林草原地區的圖們人。 “圖們人”是俄羅斯人對突厥蒙古草原遊牧民族的通用稱呼。 這些遊牧民族由庫楚姆統治，他是成吉思汗（更常見但不準確地拼寫為“根特”）汗的後代，他自稱西伯利亞汗（因此得名西伯利亞）。 當庫楚姆汗意識到俄羅斯正在堅定對上卡馬地區的控制時，他派遣一些圖們人和他們的本民族盟友，以及他的侄子馬赫梅特·庫爾來襲擊新的定居點。 圖們人屠殺了俄羅斯人（以及俄羅斯人的本民族盟友），俘虜了許多他們的婦女和兒童，然後帶著這份戰利品穿過山脈撤退。

![004](../image/turc_9781101126912_oeb_004_r1.gif)

地圖 1：俄羅斯與圖們人（十六世紀）
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

The Stroganovs 的回應是最好的防禦就是進攻。 第一步是在烏拉爾地區擴張獲得正式許可。 皇室授予了他們許可，但有條件地說，Stroganovs 完全由自己負責——他們不能指望政府提供資金或士兵。 幸運的是，他們有一個替代的招募來源——克蘇克差。 克蘇克差是居住在俄羅斯國境與克里米亞、卡贊和阿斯特拉罕汗國控制的荒野地區的粗獷俄羅斯邊疆份子。 關於他們的確切起源不清楚，但到了十六世紀，他們的主要組成成員包括逃亡農民、貧困貴族僕從和其他來自中央俄羅斯的流亡者以及他們的後代。 克蘇克差與俄羅斯國家的關係並不穩定。 作為基督教正教徒，克蘇克差通常與大主教的敵人作戰，並且經常進入政府服務。 然而，克蘇克差把自由放在一切之上，並且以發動叛亂反對中央政府而聞名。 此外，在荒野邊境上的和平貿易機會非常有限，許多克蘇克差團伙靠走私為生。

當Stroganovs 開始尋找招募人選時，他們得知一支位於伏爾加河上的盜匪團夥，其中包括埃馬克·季米里耶維奇 (Ermak Timofeev) 和伊凡·科爾索 (Ivan Koltso)。 科爾索 (“環”) 在他率領成功的襲擊莫汗汗國首都時獲得了國際名聲。 當時莫汗與俄羅斯同盟，當他們向伊凡四世（Ivan IV）投訴時，他判處科爾索死於遠方。 Stroganovs 向克蘇克差發了一封信，為公司提供了在基督教的前沿對抗“異教徒”並同時獲得大主教赦免的機會。 克蘇克差接受了這個提議。

1579 年，埃馬克的團夥到達了 Stroganov 的領土，最初作為軍事據點服役。 例如，在 1581 年夏天，他們擊敗了一支由 680 名沃古爾人 (來自烏拉爾過境的戰鬥民族烏格里克部落) 發動的襲擊行動，並俘獲了他們的領袖。 然而，他們的主要任務是將戰爭帶到敵人身上。 當代 Stroganov 日志記載了隨後發生的事件。
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

“在 1582 年 9 月 1 日，在我們聖父西門·斯提勒特、謝門、馬克斯和尼基塔·斯特羅加諾夫的聖節那天，他們派遣伏爾加酋長和科薩克人，伊瑪克·季米里耶維奇及其部隊，從他們的城市出發，反對西伯利亞蘇丹 [庫楚姆汗]。 這些人在其中有 300 名自己的士兵，由城市和列塔 [這些是一些立陶宛和德國民的戰俘，他們在成功完成事業後將獲得自由]，土耳其人和俄羅斯人，都非常勇敢。 他們團結一致地出發，與伏爾加酋長和科薩克人一起。 總共，人數為 840 名勇敢的人。 他們向全能的、聖三位的上帝以及聖母瑪利亞和所有的天使和聖徒祈禱。”

科薩克人將船隻裝滿了補給品和武器，包括火槍和輕型炮，並開始在楚索瓦亞河上向烏拉爾山脈划槳。 在他們可以到達的最遠的地方航行後，他們在烏拉爾山（該地區的山坡很平坦）上渡過河，然後在伊рты什河的支流中漂流。

“在 1582 年 9 月 9 日，在聖父雅各姆和安娜的聖節那天，這些勇敢的戰士到達了西伯利亞地區，並向圖拉河沿岸的許多土耳其人和原住民定居點發起了攻擊。 他們英勇地前往塔瓦達河，並在該河口俘獲了土耳其人戰俘。 其中一人名叫塔扎克，他是統治者 [這裡指庫楚姆汗，而不是俄羅斯統治者] 的宮廷成員；他告訴他們關於西伯利亞的沙皇和王子以及騎兵，以及庫楚姆汗。 當他們從塔扎克那里得知一切後，他們釋放了他，讓他通知蘇丹庫楚姆他們的到來、他們的實力和勇敢……

“邪惡的庫楚姆汗派遣他的兒子 [實際上是侄子] 瑪米特·庫爾與大量的戰士，命令他們英勇地抵抗入侵的俄羅斯人。 庫楚姆下令砍伐樹木並在伊рты什河的楚瓦什建造一個阿貝蒂斯，並用土地加固它，並配備防禦武器。 這將是一個重要的堡壘。

“瑪米特·庫爾及其眾多的戰士到達了巴巴桑這個地方。 俄羅斯戰士、酋長和科薩克人看到如此巨大的異教徒聚集，感到非常擔憂，但他們信任上帝並從他們的據點撤離，並襲擊了異教徒。 異教徒殘酷地從 horseback 上攻擊入侵者，並用矛和尖銳的箭射傷了科薩克人。 俄羅斯戰士還回擊 [使用火槍和輕型炮]，殺死了大量的異教徒。 俄羅斯人和土耳其人在激烈的戰鬥中傷亡慘重。 看到如此多的戰士在俄羅斯人的面前倒下，異教徒逃走了……”
```

```markdown
“當卡沙克族到達卡拉察的領土時，他們與這位對帝[庫丘姆]的顧問發生了第二次戰鬥。他們攻佔了他的領土並掠奪了他的蜂蜜和其他財物，並將其裝載到他們的船隻上。這些異教徒，在 horseback 和 foot 上追擊他們到達伊爾吞河。卡塔曼和卡沙克族勇敢地向河岸聚集的異教徒進攻，雙方在這場偉大的戰役中都損失了許多士兵喪生。然後，當異教徒看到如此多的士兵被俄羅斯勇士殺死時，他們最終逃走了。在那次戰役中，埃馬克的軍隊只失了一小部分士兵，但幾乎所有人都受了傷。

“當庫丘姆大帝看到他的士兵被壓倒時，他與一些幸存者撤退並在一個名叫楚瓦什的山坡上紮營。他的兒子馬赫梅特·庫爾留在阿巴提斯處設有一支大型後衛隊，而卡沙克族繼續沿伊爾吞河向上前進。

“當俄羅斯軍隊到達了阿迪克·穆爾所屬的一座小型聚落時，他們佔領了該聚落並在那裡紮營，因為夜已經降臨，而且一片漆黑。卡沙克族看到異教徒在他們的阿巴提斯處聚集成一團，感到非常恐慌。他們彼此說道：“我們怎麼能對抗如此眾多的敵人呢？”他們考慮了一下，然後形成一個圓圈並一起商議 [這是在卡沙克族的民主中做出決定的傳統方式]。他們辯論。“我們應該撤退，還是像一體一樣團結抵抗？”有些人沉思並且認為：“對我們來說最好是撤退。”但另一些人堅定不移且堅決地宣布：“啊，兄弟戰友們，我們怎麼能逃跑呢？秋天已經來臨了。河流中的冰正在結冰。我們無法逃跑並為自己帶來恥辱和 disgrace 。相反，讓我們把我們的信任放在上帝身上，因為勝利並不是來自於擁有大量的士兵，而是來自上帝的幫助。”即使是弱小的人也能得到上帝的幫助。兄弟們，我們自己沒有聽說過這個無神教且被詛咒的西伯利亞人，庫丘姆大帝，給俄羅斯彼爾姆地區帶來的邪惡，他摧毀了我們的主[俄羅斯皇帝]的城市，殺害並奴役了正統基督徒嗎？我們知道斯特羅甘諾夫堡壘被他摧毀了多少個嗎？至高無上的三位一體的上帝會懲罰這個被詛咒的人為灑下基督教的血。”他們說：“兄弟們，讓我們回憶起我們的誓言，我們在誠實的人[斯特羅甘諾夫]面前，向上帝所宣誓的誓言。我們發誓並親吻了十字架，如果至高無上的上帝幫助我們，即使我們死得徹底，我們也不會撤退。我們不能後退。我們不能羞辱自己並打破我們所宣誓的誓言。如果至高無上的三位一體的上帝幫助我們，即使我們倒下，我們的記憶也不會消失在這些土地上，我們的榮耀將永遠存在！”
```

```markdown
“聽聞此言，亞坦曼和科薩克人精神大振，勇氣也重燃。他們一同高聲發誓：「我們準備為聖教會而死。我們將為真正東正教受苦。我們將效忠虔誠的君主大公伊凡·瓦西里維奇以及俄羅斯的一切 [伊萬四世]。我們將堅定抵抗異教徒至最後一滴血，直至死亡本身。兄弟們，我們絕不背叛誓言，我們如一體而立，堅定不移！」…

“他們於十月二十三日，聖使雅各的節日（我們的主之弟兄）從營地出發前往戰鬥。他們一同高聲呼喊：「上帝與我們同在！主啊，幫助我們，你們的卑微僕人們！」

“他們勇敢而無畏地向障柵前進，並與異教徒展開了激烈的戰鬥。異教徒從障柵頂端和炮口射出無數箭矢，傷害了許多艾馬克的勇士，並殺死了另一些人。當他們看到這些勇士倒下時，異教徒通過障柵三個地點發動突襲，企圖迫使科薩克人逃兵。在這些突襲中，他們奮力搏鬥，近身格鬥。

“科薩克人如同一個人向前衝擊異教徒，證明了他們在神 disgraced  disgraced and godless heathen面前的勇敢和兇猛。終於，異教徒的力量衰竭，上帝賜給科薩克人勝利。科薩克人贏得了地利，擊敗了異教徒，殺死了眾多的人。他們將他們從障柵上驅趕，並在上面豎立了自己的戰旗。他們傷害了馬赫梅特·庫爾，他的士兵們乘坐一艘小船橫渡伊рты斯河將他帶走。

“ camped on the hill, 看到他的塔塔르人被擊敗，以及他的兒子馬赫梅特·庫爾受傷逃亡。 他命令他的穆拉德呼喚他們可恥的伊斯蘭禱文。 他向他的邪惡神靈祈求幫助，但沒有得到任何援助。 同時，奧斯提亞克公爵們 [塔塔爾人的本底盟友] 也帶領他們的士兵撤退，儘管他們可以……

“這個可憐的統治者駕馬奔馳到他的城市西伯，並帶走了一部分財富，然後繼續逃亡，留下西伯市荒廢。 勇敢的艾馬克和他的隊伍於十月二十六日，聖殉道者狄米特里奧斯（沙龍尼加）的節日到達了西伯，後來稱為托博爾斯克。他們感謝上帝賜給他們在無神之徒和詛咒的異教徒身上取得勝利，並歡欣鼓舞。他們奪取了大量的黃金、白銀、黃布、寶石、水貂、狐狸和有價值的動物，並將這些東西分享給彼此。”
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

“這非常值得一提，而且確實榮耀了全能的三位一體上帝，他賦予了小但堅強的俄羅斯戰士們在異教徒面前取得勝利，並擊敗了傲慢的庫丘姆大公。庫丘姆大公聚集了一支人數遠多於克蘇克人的軍隊，比例為 10 比 20 或甚至 30 比 1。這個被詛咒的人哀嘆他許多戰士中倒下了。因此，上帝降伏了傲慢之人，並偏愛謙卑的基督徒。”

“這位伊爾馬克的征服西伯利亞的故事，正如由當代史官所記載的，不僅因為它所描述的事件而引人入勝，也因為它的敘述方式而有趣。史官對這個故事所施加的意識形態色彩提供了一個了解俄羅斯人如何看待他們與塔塔爾人的衝突，以及在推進俄羅斯邊疆的人們的動機的線索。但首先讓我們關注事件的基本框架。一支由幾百名勇敢的歐洲探險家組成的團體擊敗了大量的原住民，征服了一個國度，並掠奪了一大批財寶。伊爾馬克的克蘇克人與在美洲發現皮薩羅或比薩索等征服者之間存在著驚人的相似之處（儘管，當然，皮薩羅所掠奪的財寶遠超過伊爾馬克在西伯利亞可能找到的任何數量）。”
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

如何達成？ Jared Diamond 最近透過解釋柯爾特斯和皮薩羅的壯舉，認為西班牙人擁有槍械、疾病和鋼鐵，而沒有與1492年之前沒有與歐亞大陸通訊的美國原住民有任何接觸。 這種解釋對於西班牙征服美洲來說合理，但無法幫助我們理解俄羅斯的西伯利亞征服。 我們可以立即否定 Diamond 的三要素的三分之二，因為雙方在幾個世紀以來都暴露於相同的疾病和鋼鐵之中。 就槍械而言，俄羅斯人有效地將其用於對使用弓箭的遊牧民族的反擊。 但為什麼俄羅斯能夠裝備槍械，而圖們察人卻不能？ 這兩種族群都不是火器發明的創造者。（事實上，圖們察人在從中國這兩個發明者那裡直接獲得火藥方面處於更佳地位。） 一種帶有偏見的解釋，強調歐洲人和非歐洲人的差異，是不令人滿意的，因為其他突厥人——鄂圖曼人和摩爾人——熱衷地採用火器並有效地利用它們來建立龐大的帝國。 在西伯利亞表親的西南方一千英里處的克里米亞圖們察人於 1530 年左右開始使用攻城武器和手持槍械。 無論如何，在西伯利亞戰役中，火器所扮演的角色非常微小。 科薩克人的原始匹配式火炮緩慢發射、準確性不足且無法在潮濕天氣中使用。 實際上，十五世紀和十六世紀的火藥革命的主要影響是火炮能夠摧毀中世紀的堡壘。 手持槍械直到十七世紀才真正有效，隨著曲柄點火步槍的發明。
```

```markdown
## 文件路徑：Document

當我們考慮在伊瑪克的數百年之前，東歐發生的事情時，謎團更加深重。於 1236 年，由拔都率領的蒙古大軍入侵者，拔都曾是成吉思汗的孫子，在伊爾帖河西部的草原上集結，這個區域後來在三個多世紀後成為西伯利亞汗國。儘管我們稱他們為蒙古人，但民族蒙古人僅佔總兵力的一 tenth； 其餘則是由各種突厥族人主導的部落混合體，包括喀喇支、圖特（俄羅斯人將其名稱擴展以涵蓋所有種族突厥-蒙古的草原人）、烏育兒、許瓦米亞人、土庫曼人等。蒙古對東歐的征服始於對波羅茨葉爾格人的毀滅。從 1237 年開始，持續三年，蒙古人系統地征服了幾乎整個俄羅斯。（僅諾夫哥羅德在西北部逃脫了直接攻擊，但仍然不得不向拔都臣服並同意支付貢賦。）這次征服最顯著的方面是，儘管每個公國都勇敢地反抗入侵者，但俄羅斯人卻無法團結起來對抗蒙古人的威脅。這種合作無果的情況在兩個兄弟尤里和羅曼的故事中得到了最生動的體現，他們統治著莫斯科以東南部的瑞잔公國。當蒙古軍隊逼近時，尤里把自己鎖在瑞잔公國的首府瑞잔，而羅曼則不來幫助他的兄弟，而是待在瑞잔西北方 50 英里的較小鎮科洛姆納。蒙古人首先攻陷瑞잔，殺害了尤里，並屠殺了整個人口。然後他們前往科洛姆納，在堡壘前擊敗和殺死了羅曼，並佔領了科洛姆納本身。

同樣的故事一遍又一遍地重複發生。俄羅斯分裂成數十個小公國，以及俄羅斯人無法團結起來對抗外部威脅，是導致蒙古人在 13世紀征服俄羅斯的主要原因（也許是主要原因）。這種缺陷對俄羅斯人自己來說也十分明顯，正如在蒙古征服後不久所作的《關於俄羅斯土地的衰亡之歌》中所清楚地表明。

相比之下，蒙古人擅長團隊合作。歷史學家普遍認為，蒙古人能夠壓倒所有敵人並非由於任何武器技術上的優勢，也並非由於他們的數量。（他們經常與和摧毀了人數上優勢的敵人作戰。）尋找蒙古成功的原因必須在其他地方。
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

The蒙古軍隊是一個經過良好運作的社會機制，能夠在紀律和內在凝聚力方面達到自古羅馬以來歐洲未曾見及的程度。蒙古軍隊部署、進攻和行軍時，幾乎沒有聲音，甚至沒有命令吶喊，因為騎兵方陣的移動都由標準旗手發出的旗號來控制。當到來適當的時刻，整支軍隊突然衝鋒，像惡魔一樣嘶吼和尖叫。這種戰術對他們的敵人來說極其令人不安。

蒙古人最喜歡使用的伎倆之一是假撤退，引誘不明智的敵人進入埋伏和消滅。運用這類戰術，需要一支由10萬人組成的軍隊，需要精確的時間控制和無縫合作。另一種戰術，由教皇使節皮亞諾·卡皮尼描述如下：“他們用囚犯和外國遊兵組成的前線衝擊蒙古騎兵，而他們的兵力主力則在兩翼上部署，以便包抄敵人。他們做到如此有效，使敵人誤以為他們比實際人數更多。如果敵方奮力抵抗，他們就會打開陣勢，讓其逃脫，然後追擊並殺死盡可能多的逃兵。”世界歷史學家威廉·麥尼爾指出：“蒙古人能夠在各種地形上移動，同時保持各個軍隊之間的溝通，以確保在決定性的時間和地點集中所有力量。1241年入侵歐洲的總指揮薩博泰毫無顧忌地協調了在波蘭運營的軍隊與壓向匈牙利的軍隊，儘管卡爾帕阡山脈阻隔了它們，但沒有其他歐洲軍隊直到19世紀後期才實現如此可比的協調能力。”

蒙古人的統一目標從大型軍事單位的移動延伸到人際關係。正如來自法國法庭的大使威廉·德·魯布魯克所報告的：“在世界上，沒有像土耳其人那樣更聽話的臣民，無論是平民還是僧侶，他們對自己的領主表現出比任何其他人的更多尊重，幾乎不敢向他們撒謊。他們很少互相辱罵，如果他們這樣做了，爭端從未引發打鬥。在他們之間沒有發生戰爭、爭吵、肉體傷害和謀殺，也沒有大規模的盜賊或搶劫犯。”正是這種非凡的社會凝聚力解釋了蒙古人在從朝鮮到匈牙利的對抗所有其他歐亞軍隊中取得的輝煌成就。
```

```markdown
SECTION PATH: Document

THE CHARACTERIZATION OF THE MONGOLS that stresses their ability to cooperate will probably sound strange to many readers. Cooperation is a “nice” word, and the Mongols of Chinggis Khan were most definitely not nice people. They slaughtered literally millions of men, women, and children, and enslaved millions of survivors. They turned dozens of wealthy and beautiful cities into ruins and piled pyramids of hundreds of thousands of skulls as grisly monuments to their achievements. They practiced cruel executions and unspeakable tortures on those unlucky to fall into their hands. And wasn’t the empire of Chinggis Khan a typical “oriental despotism”? So how is it possible to speak about the spirit of cooperation in such a society?

This is a very important question because, as discussed in subsequent chapters, cooperation, or more generally the capacity for collective action, is a key factor in the rise of empires. It must be noted immediately that the concept of oriental despotism, if it means the absolute power of one individual over the whole society, is a sociological nonsense. A single person, no matter how physically impressive, cannot rule against the wishes of all of his subjects. As soon as he falls asleep, one of the people he has oppressed will end his tyranny by sticking a knife in him. In real life, tyrants could rule only because they had the support of a certain group of people—the palace guard, the aristocracy, perhaps the top bureaucrats. Only groups can oppress other groups and whole societies, and to do that the “oppressor” group must be internally cohesive. In other words, oppression can only be accomplished from the basis of cooperation, paradoxical as it sounds.

The social matrix of Western societies (weaved from such things as education, mass media, and even cocktail-party chitchat) conditions us to think that the only legitimate source of social power is “we the people.” As a corollary, we tend to assume that nondemocratic societies are held together by force alone. A recent illustration of this pervasive cultural bias is the implicit assumption by the American planners of the Iraq invasion in 2003 that as soon as Saddam Hussein was overthrown by American troops, the Iraqi people would work together with the occupation authorities in building a democratic society.
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

There is no question that the Ba‘athist regime of Saddam Hussein used violence and intimidation to keep down dissident groups, and the many atrocities committed by Saddam’s henchmen are well documented. However, this was not the whole story. In addition to force, the regime relied on cooperation from certain other groups: the core support came from Saddam’s clan, with the wider power base provided by the Sunni Arabs of Iraq. In addition, a more diffuse group, originating from other ethnic segments of the Iraqi population (the Shiite Arabs and the Sunni Kurds and Turkmen), had come to think of themselves as “Iraqis” first and members of their ethnic group second. Although this group, let us loosely call them nationalists, did not actively support the Ba’athist regime, they acquiesced to its rule. Although perhaps not holding the legitimacy of Saddam’s government terribly high, many of them consider the legitimacy of the occupying powers to be even lower.

We now know empirically that Saddam’s regime was not based solely on force, because many members of the groups that supported him when he was in power are still willing to sacrifice their lives attacking his captors (even after Saddam himself has become powerless). An even greater number participates in demonstrations and other acts of nonviolent resistance, an activity that, although not as suicidal as direct attacks against the well-armed American troops, is by no means risk-free. Finally, the majority of Iraqis have just chosen to have as little to do with the American authorities as possible. During the first months of the occupation, various commentators attributed this aloofness to the residual fear that Saddam could yet return to power and punish those who cooperated with the Americans. However, the capture of Saddam in late 2003 did not change Iraqi attitudes in any significant way.

The case of Ba’athist Iraq, thus, serves as an excellent illustration of the idea that oppression and cooperation are not mutually exclusive—to oppress the dissidents, Saddam had to have cooperation within his social power base. To the Bush administration, Saddam was a murderous thug, a tin-pot dictator, a failed and incompetent Hitler wannabe. But he can also be seen as a stern and wily tribal leader, who bestowed rich rewards on his people, while meting out harsh punishment to their enemies. The brutality of his secret service, of his sons, and of his very own actions can be seen as strength. Certainly this is how a significant minority of Iraqis saw him. And they were prepared to cooperate with him.
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

如何良好地與東歐的十六世紀葉爾羌人合作？請記住，西伯利亞汗國的葉爾羌人在三個多世紀前由拔都率領的圖古蒙古軍隊征服東歐的土著後代。例如，庫楚木汗是成吉思汗氏族成員，他的祖先可以追溯到拔都的兄弟賽班。然而，這些後來的人類與他們的祖先截然不同。儘管擁有巨大的數量優勢，但他們無法擊敗伊馬克的科薩克人。

更重要的是，在十六世紀，各種葉爾羌公國未能團結起來反對捲土重來的俄羅斯。當蒙古帝國被四個成吉思汗分支劃分時，拔都及其後代獲得最西部的部分並將首都設於下伏爾加河畔的薩雷，而“黃金帳”軍團（即拔都的領域）在歷史上維持了統一200年，僅在十四世紀末經歷了一段內戰時期。十五世紀中葉，它分裂成多個獨立公國：卡扎尼汗國、阿斯特蘭汗國、克里米亞汗國和西伯利亞汗國，以及諾蓋汗國。這些黃金帳軍團的繼承國並不穩定，並在十六世紀繼續遭受內戰的蹂蝨。卡扎尼公國中的貴族派系不斷進行政變。其中一位競爭對手的王子沙阿里首先奪取王位，然後又三度失去王位！西伯利亞汗國也經歷了一系列內戰。最後一次內戰，1563-9年，庫楚木汗擊敗並殺死了西伯利亞汗國的前任汗，僅在俄羅斯入侵前12年結束。因此，我們所看到的是與三個多世紀前的情況完全相反的情況。現在輪到葉爾羌人體驗在俄羅斯統治下社會瓦解。

同時，黃金帳軍團分裂時，俄羅斯土地也在莫斯科的領導下緩慢但不可避免地“匯集”，正如俄羅斯史料記載的那樣。這個過程於1485年基本完成，莫斯科吞併了最後一個獨立公國特弗爾。這種解體趨勢，具有蒙古征服前俄羅斯的特徵，完全被逆轉了。當一塊領土添加到莫斯科公國中時，它就會停留在那裡。這種中心化、整合的趨勢即使在公國擴張到核心俄羅斯土地之外（1552-56年，通過征服卡扎尼和阿斯特蘭汗國）後仍然存在。領土獲取的堅韌性可以用以下事件來說明：在西伯利亞戰役之後發生的事件。
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

After wintering in Sibir, Ermak sent his lieutenant, Ivan Koltso, “the Ring,” with the report of their great victory back across the Urals. The news that another kingdom was added to the Russian Empire was met with great popular jubilation. Koltso received a pardon for his crimes and rich gifts from the hands of the tsar himself, and left to Sibir accompanied by a company of government troops. Although the conquest of Sibir started as a private action, neither Ermak nor the Stroganovs considered establishing an independent princedom in Siberia for themselves. Whether their offering of Siberia to the tsar was born of loyalty or calculation, the subsequent course of events showed the wisdom of this course of action.

Although he lost the battle of Sibir, Kuchum Khan did not give up the struggle. The Tatars, however, were plagued by dissent. Several Tatar nobles and their following deserted Kuchum and went over to the son of the previous khan (whom Kuchum had killed in the civil war). Lacking strong forces to dislodge the Cossacks, Kuchum shifted to guerilla tactics. His nephew Mahmet-Kul succeeded in inflicting some casualties on the Russians, but was eventually captured and sent to Moscow. During the second winter, however, the Cossacks ran out of supplies and began suffering from scurvy and starvation. Then disaster struck in the summer of 1584: At night, the Tatars attacked the camp where Ermak and his comrades slept. Most of the Cossacks were killed, and Ermak himself drowned while attempting to swim to the boats in the river. News of Ermak’s death was the final straw for the defenders of Sibir. Their numbers had been whittled down by constant Tatar attacks, and it was clear that they could not survive a third winter. The Russians were forced to retreat across the Urals to the Stroganov lands, and Kuchum reoccupied Sibir.

Unfortunately for the Tatars, their ultimate defeat was only postponed. Two years later, the Russians entered Siberia again. They proceeded in a systematic fashion, first building the fortified town of Tyumen (1586); then Tobolsk (1587), near the site of recaptured Sibir; Tara (1594); and, finally, Surgut, on the Ob River (also in 1594). Kuchum fought on for years, but was defeated in a final battle on the Ob in 1598. He took refuge with the Nogay, where he was assassinated in 1600.
```

```markdown
## 文件路徑：Document

THE OVERARCHING QUESTION OF THIS BOOK is why do large empires rise and fall? Therefore, it is only proper to start with the struggle between the people who built the two largest territorial empires ever seen in world history. When we stand back and take a long view at the course of this struggle, we are struck by the complete reversal in the fortunes of these two nations. In the thirteenth century, Russia, fragmented into a multitude of bickering principalities, had no chance against the Mongol steamroller. In the sixteenth century, it was the turn of the Russian monolith to roll over the squabbling Tatar khanates. Why did the Tatars lose their social cohesion? How did the Russians acquire it?

Social cohesion, of course, is not the only factor we will need to explain the rise and fall of empires. History is too complex for single-factor explanations. It is clear, however, that social cohesion, or lack of it, played a large role in the stunning reversal of fortune in the centuries-long Russian-Tatar struggle. What made Russia evolve from a collection of bickering principalities to a highly centralized state?

第二章

邊緣生活

俄羅斯——及美國 的轉變

塑造俄羅斯歷史的最重要因素之一是它位於歐洲的廣闊草原的前沿。 數個世紀以來，從西南部的基輔到東北部的卡贊的一條線將兩個截然不同的世界分隔開來。 在該線的北部和西部是居住在斯拉夫、巴爾幹和烏格里克人的森林地區，他們以農業為主，並通過狩獵和採集進行補充； 而位於該線的南部和東部則是居住在遊牧民族及其牲畜的草原地區。  πρώτοι 遊牧民——迦米雷人、斯基泰人和薩爾馬提亞人——使用印歐語。 然而，從公元三世紀開始，這些印歐語遊牧民被來自中亞的重複波浪般的土耳其人和蒙古人所取代。

森林農民和草原遊牧民族之間存在著深厚的文化隔閡。 對於遊牧民來說，農民是卑賤的人，做女性的工作，笨拙的騎手，在戰鬥中又弱小而膽怯。 然而，農民擁有遊牧民渴望的東西——穀物，他們無法自己種植； 貴族和祭司積累的財富，以及最後但非最不重要的，他們的身體，可以在黑海奴隸市場上出售。
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

從農民的角度來看，遊牧民族是惡魔騎士，野蠻、無學識的異族，殺戮者、奴隸販賣者和破壞者。農民與放牧者的敵對關係可以追溯到人類歷史的開端，如《創世記》中該隱（以田地為生）與雅各布（以羊群為生）之間的衝突故事所展現。(因為早期的希伯來人是放牧者，自然故事中的壞傢伙就是該隱。) 在東歐，從十世紀開始，定居農民的傾向於接受基督教，而遊牧民族則傾向於伊斯蘭教，進一步加深了文化鴻溝。在俄羅斯史料中描述遊牧民族（例如“無神者”或“異教徒”）最常用的術語反映了這一宗教界限。  incidentally, 在現代俄語中，“異教徒”一詞已經失去了其原始的宗教意義，現在只表示“壞”或“邪惡”。 如前章所述，關於俄羅斯人和圖赤之間衝突的宗教方面在斯特羅甘諾夫史料對他們之間的戰鬥描述中體現出來。

氣候和生態界限將草原與森林連接起來，成為兩個截然不同的文明之間的一個重要分歧線。 在這個分歧線上互動受到兩種基本事實的影響：首先，遊牧民族擁有豐富的動物產品，但植物產品卻稀缺；人類不能只靠肉類生存。其次，他們的武藝很強。由於在追逐和保護牲畜免受掠食者侵害的日常練習中，騎射技術得到了充分發展，因此遊牧民族在軍事上對定居人口具有顯著優勢。 遊牧民族對糧食的需求以及他們能夠通過暴力奪取它所帶來的能力不可避免地導致了他們與農民之間的敵對關係。 這並不意味著農牧互動總是充滿戰爭色彩。 在某些條件下，遊牧民族可以通過和平貿易獲取所需（尤其是在強大國家保護下）。 農業文明和遊牧文明的交易採取了各種形式。 有時甚至發生聯姻，通常在貴族層面。
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

On the fault line between the eastern Slavs and their steppe neighbors, however, the dominant factor was conflict. The intensity of the conflict fluctuated across the centuries, but periodically it reached the level of genocide. One of the relatively peaceful periods was the first half of the eleventh century, when the principality of Kiev was at the height of its power. The strong and unified state was able to reduce the threat from the steppe to a minimum. Unfortunately, toward the end of the eleventh century, the principality began fragmenting, a process that coincided with the arrival of a new wave of Turkic nomads in the Russian steppes, the Cumans. The Russian chronicles record 46 Cuman invasions into the principality between 1061 and 1200. During the twelfth century, as a result of internecine fighting and the Cuman raids, the population of Kiev and the surrounding territories collapsed. The Mongol sack in 1240 struck the deathblow. From that time until the seventeenth century, the core territory of the Kievan state was virtually a desert. Any Ukrainian peasant foolish enough to move into it was immediately killed, and his family taken to the Crimean slave markets, by the first marauding Tatar band that would chance upon them.

The thirteenth century depopulation affected not only Kiev, but also the entire forest-steppe transition zone. As a result of increased pressure from the steppe, the cultural fault line was pushed a hundred miles or more to the northwest. In the Russian principality of Ryazan (where the two brothers, Yurii and Roman, would not work together to repel the Mongols), the capital city of Ryazan was too close to the steppe and had to be abandoned. The princely seat was moved to Pereyaslavl-Ryazansky in the northwest corner of the principality.

Life settled down a bit under the Golden Horde, whose rulers were more interested in getting tribute than in murder and rapine. The population of northern Russia enjoyed a substantial recovery, despite the effects of a few punitive expeditions by the Tatars in response to urban uprisings against their tax collectors. As the Golden Horde began fragmenting during the fifteenth century, however, the ability of its rulers to restrain raiding by lower-level chieftains waned. When the Golden Horde experienced its ultimate collapse around 1500, Muscovite lands faced an increasing number of raids from the Tatar successor states. (Muscovy is what historians call Russia during the period after the independence from the Golden Horde, but before the reign of Peter the Great, which started the Imperial period.) The greatest danger came from the Kazan khanate, until it was conquered in 1552, and from the Crimean Tatars, who were to remain a thorn in Russia’s side until the end of the eighteenth century.
```

```markdown
## 文件路徑：Document

The devastation caused by the Tatar attacks was huge. In 1521, the Crimean Khan Mohammad-Girey, with a 100,000-man army, broke through the Russian defenses along the Oka River and invaded the Muscovite heartland. He did not attempt to assault the fortified cities, but instead laid waste to the countryside. The worst damage resulted from the enormous number of people the Tatars carried away. According to one chronicle, captives numbered 300,000; the imperial envoy Sigismund von Herberstein reported that total losses numbered 800,000 people, some slain, others sold to the Turks in Caffa (in Crimea). Herberstein’s report must be greatly exaggerated, but the loss of even 200,000 or 300,000 people was a very serious blow to a country whose total population at the time was only 7 million. In 1533, the Crimean Tatars failed to break through the Oka defenses and had to content themselves with devastating the Ryazan lands. Nevertheless, the Tatars again carried away a multitude of captives. In a letter to the tsar, the khan boasted that Russia lost no fewer than 100,000 of its people: Every Tatar noble acquired 15 to 20 captives; the common warriors each held 5 or 6 “heads.”

These two invasions were not unique, only the more successful of many other raids. Few were the years during the first half of the sixteenth century when Muscovy was not assaulted by the Crimeans from the south and the Kazan Tatars from the east. Just during the 1530s, for example, no fewer than 13 Crimean and 20 Kazan raids occurred. Added to that were raids from the Nogay Horde, and on the western frontier Muscovy was embroiled in a long and exhausting conflict with Lithuania.

Muscovy could resist the onslaught from the steppe only by a concerted effort of the whole people, from the mighty boyar to the lowest peasant. A characteristic example of how the external threat helped to unify the society was the construction of the fortified town of Lyubim on the frontier facing Kazan, in an area that did not have a stronghold where peasants could shelter during the Tatar raids. The central government had no resources to spare, and therefore gave permission to build using local resources. Everybody pitched in to help quarry the stone, raise the walls, dig the moat, and make the defensive stakes against the cavalry. Another sign of the willingness of people to sacrifice for the sake of the larger community was the periodic collections of money needed to buy out the Russian captives. Enormous sums of money were gathered in this way, and as a result many thousands of captives were able to return home.
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

The main role in organizing the defense, however, fell to the state. The government first fortified the southern frontier along the Oka, which faced the Crimean raids. Stone fortresses were constructed at key defensive points. All fords and other places where the Tatar cavalry could cross the river were blocked with wooden stockades manned by soldiers and artillery. Every summer, large bodies of armed men gathered at several designated places, from where they could be rushed to any threatened segment of the frontier. The Cossacks patrolled the lands beyond the Oka to give an early warning of the approaching raiders. By the mid-1520s, the system of defenses was in place and all of its elements well coordinated. In 1527, the campaign of the whole Crimean army in Russia failed completely because the Tatars were unable to penetrate the Oka barrier.

The eastern frontier enjoyed no natural defensive feature such as the Oka, and therefore the defenses against Kazan were ineffective. The Tatars just bypassed the fortresses and devastated the fields and villages, killing or carrying off those souls who were caught in the open. Many of the survivors migrated west to escape the constant danger. Tatar raiding was systematically depopulating the broad band of territory between Moscow and Kazan. It was clear that the only way to avoid the fate of Kiev three centuries before was to solve the problem at its source. Therefore, after the defenses of the southern frontier began functioning properly, the government directed all of its resources to the east. It took two decades of constant war, and a final lengthy siege, but Muscovy succeeded in annexing the khanate of Kazan in 1552.
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

儘管1556年吞併卡잔，隨後又吞併阿斯特蘭汗，解決了東部邊疆的問題，但奧卡防禦線只提供南部的暫時解決方案。第一個問題是，該防禦線僅距離莫斯科 50 英里 southward，因此草原遊牧人的任何突破都立即暴露內陸地區於掠奪和破壞之中。第二個問題是，現在屬於莫斯科的基輔羅莎的前兩個公國——瑞잔和諾夫哥羅德-謝爾斯基，仍然位於防禦線之外且容易受到土耳其人襲擊。第三個問題，是一個重複出現的問題，即一旦建立安全的防禦線，俄羅斯農民就會開始向其前方移動（儘管當局試圖阻止這種自發的殖民化，因為他們無法有效保護這些先鋒），這為當局帶來了許多挑戰，但沒有直接產生稅收收益（至少在最初的時候）。然而，壓制殖民化的努力卻是無效的。隨著防禦線以外的人口增加，它吸引了土耳其人的襲擊隊伍，並發出保護“基督教靈魂”的呼籲。政府被迫動員資源來建造新的防禦線，位於向南，以保護新殖民的領土。在確保該領土之後，政府官員可以計算人口並賦予每位家庭長老其在邊境防禦力量中的稅收和服務份額，最終，殖民化運動對政府有利。然而，這個過程又會重新開始，當農民開始向新的線條中滲透時。結果是一個奇怪的自發性動態，在這個動態中，普通人民和國家共同努力（雖然他們可能沒有意識到）將莫斯科的領土向南延伸至草原，在若干步驟中進行。這個過程最終只在征服克里米亞之後才結束，即兩個半世紀 спустя.

STEPPE 邊疆的生活狀況如何？ 文檔來源提供了很好的見解，而且這些來源在16世紀和17世紀的後期變得越來越好。 我們還很幸運地擁有由Guillaume le Vasseur, Sieur de Beauplan撰寫的一本書，他在1630年至1647年間在烏克蘭邊疆地區（當時是波蘭-立陶宛的一部分）度過了時間。 Beauplan 為我們提供了關於俄羅斯人和利特瓦人長期進行的艱苦鬥爭對手的寶貴信息。
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

The khanate of Crimea enjoyed an advantageous geopolitical situation, which explains why the contest between it and Muscovy took three centuries to resolve. Its capital, Bakhchisarai, was located on the Crimean Peninsula, which could be attacked only after crossing an easily defended Isthmus of Perekop. Even more important was the control by the Crimeans of the huge steppe territory of southern Russia. These steppes created a buffer zone hundreds of miles deep, a zone easily crossed by the Tatar cavalry, but extremely difficult to penetrate with a European-style army composed primarily of foot soldiers and burdened by heavy supply carts.

Although Bakhchisarai was the political capital of the Crimean khanate, the most economically important city in Crimea was Caffa. Caffa 該城市與歐洲歷史上的一些最黑暗的頁面相關。在 1346 年，當卡法由熱那亞人控制時，蒙古人圍攻該市。當包圍者因新從中亞抵達的疾病而死亡時，他們將多個患病屍體投射入城市，然後離開。一年內，該疾病從卡法傳播到所有主要的地中海港口。在接下來的三年裡，歐洲人口的一半死於鼠疫（又稱黑死病）疫情。

The Ukrainians referred to Caffa as “the vampire that drinks the blood of Russia” because both under the Genoese and after its conquest by the Turks this port city was the main entrepôt for the slave trade on the Black Sea. Over the centuries, literally millions of eastern Slavs and other peoples inhabiting the forest region north of the steppe were sold in Caffa and shipped to a variety of destinations in the Mediterranean. Most male slaves sold in Caffa probably ended up rowing the galleys. At any given time during the seventeenth century, the city had 30,000 or more slaves. The supply of slaves was so plentiful that there were no free domestic servants in Caffa.

In the second half of the fifteenth century, the Genoese lost Caffa to the Ottoman Empire. The Turks governed Caffa directly, and also exercised an indirect control over the rest of the peninsula, because in 1475 the khan of Crimea became the vassal of the sultan. However, the Turkish-supplied artillery and janissaries became involved only in large-scale military operations against Russia and Poland-Lithuania, leaving the usual steppe raiding entirely in the hands of the Tatars. The Crimean army consisted of 40,000 to 50,000 horse warriors. When allies from other hordes and various other volunteer predators joined this army, its size could swell to 100,000 and more. However, a more typical raid was conducted with “only” 15,000 to 20,000 horsemen led by one of the khan’s murzas (a Tatar princeling).
```

```markdown
## 文件路徑: Document

Beauplan 記錄稱，每個塔塔戰士都配備兩匹備用馬；因此，一支 80,000 人的大軍 сопровожда著超過 200,000 頭的馬。 “森林裡的樹木比平原上在同一時間的馬還要少，而且從遠處看去，它們看起來像一團從地平線上升起的雲朵，隨著上升而越來越大，給甚至是最勇敢的人們也帶來恐懼，如果他們不習慣看到如此眾多的軍隊聚集在一起。” 在波蘭-立陶宛烏克蘭邊境，該地區缺乏莫斯科人所建造的系統防禦，塔塔軍隊的一種典型戰術是首先迅速滲透到定居區深處。 達到 60 或 80 英里（1 英里等於 3 英里）的內陸後，軍隊會逆向返回，左右兩側的翼線延伸 8 到 12 英里，並開始對該地區進行有系統的清剿以搜刮財物。 所有抵抗者都會被殺死；其他人則被俘虜並帶走（包括牲畜，除了豬）。

在一次成功的行動之後，當塔塔人遠離邊境到草原上，以至於不用擔心追擊時，他們會停下來休息和重新組織。 “在此一周的停歇期間，他們會把所有的財物都集中起來，這些財物由奴隸和牲畜組成，並將整個數量平均分配給自己。 任何冷酷無情的心靈都會被看到丈夫與妻子分開、母親與女兒分開所觸動，而且他們永遠不會再見面的希望渺茫。 他們將成為穆斯林教徒的 wretched 奴隸，他們會殘暴地虐待他們。 [這些塔塔人的] 殘酷行為導致他們犯下無數卑鄙行徑，例如掠奪年輕女孩、在丈夫和父親面前強姦婦女，甚至在父母面前切除男孩的陰莖，以便他們可以獻給穆罕默德。”

當塔塔軍隊與波蘭軍隊相遇時，他們避免與其交戰，因為 “這些搶劫犯（因此應該稱他們為搶劫犯）從未 [烏克蘭]  raiding 的目的是為了戰鬥，而是為了伏擊和偷竊。” 遊牧騎兵所享有的巨大優勢是隱蔽、靈活性和出乎意料。 防禦他們的掠奪行為非常困難，事實上，烏克蘭人和波蘭人與俄國人不同，無法對克里米亞人造成進攻。 當 16世紀後期塔塔人的壓力加劇時，烏克蘭甚至失去了一些地盤。 例如，1578 年至 1583 年期間，位於德涅斯特河和多涅茨河之間的波多利亞省的全部三分之一村莊被摧毀或廢棄了。
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

The key feature of the Muscovite frontier strategy was the construction of fortified defensive lines that extended across hundreds of miles of the steppe. I have already discussed the first defensive line along the Oka River. The need to protect Ryazan and Novgorod-Severski, as well as territories newly colonized by peasants moving from the north, was addressed by the construction of the second defensive line in the 1560s and 1570s. The line ran through a chain of fortified towns, whose function was not economic, but purely defensive. In forested areas between the fortresses, obstacles were constructed by felling trees. Trees were cut at two yards above the ground, and placed with their crowns pointing south. Interweaved trunks and branches, backed up by two-yard tree stumps, presented an impenetrable barrier to mounted men. Dismantling this barrier would take hours, giving the Cossacks and soldiers more time to organize a proper “reception” for the unwanted guests. The main purpose of such abatis was not to prevent entry, but to negate the raiders’ advantage in mobility. The obstacles also impeded rapid retreat of the Tatars laden with loot, cattle, and captives. Slowing their flight even by a few hours could allow the pursuit to catch up, spelling the difference between freedom and slavery for the unfortunates who were caught out in the open during the raid.

In areas without forests, the Russians pounded logs into the ground to construct palisades. Wherever possible, rivers were utilized to serve as obstacles. (Unfortunately, no convenient large river ran from west to east, such as the Oka, on which the old defensive line was based.) The forests growing along the defensive lines were strictly protected against cutting. All measures, no matter how petty, were taken to impede the raiders. For example, the grass south of the line was burned after the frost in late fall to deny fodder to the Tatar horses.
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

The length of the second defensive line was more than 600 miles, a Russian equivalent of the Great Wall of China, fulfilling the same function albeit with very different construction methods. The investment of labor was enormous. Tens of thousands of people, mostly drawn from the frontier population, worked on the construction. The frontiersmen expended a remarkable effort, but it could not have happened without the full backing of the central government, which founded fortified towns on the steppe, recruited the garrisons from the central areas of Muscovy, and provided overall organization. The key role of the central government is highlighted by the occasions when the defenses failed, which always happened either when the authorities were preoccupied with the war on the western frontier or during the Time of Troubles (when the central government collapsed). In 1571, the Tatars broke through the defenses and succeeded in burning Moscow. The last time the Tatars managed to reach Moscow and burn its suburbs was in 1592. Successful raids reached the Muscovite heartland in the first half of the seventeenth century, but after the 1650s the Tatar raids were no longer able to penetrate the defense lines, which by that time had moved even farther south.

The organization of the frontier service was perfected during the sixteenth century. The first line of defenses consisted of Cossack patrols deep into the steppe. In one typical technique, a pair of sentries stationed themselves near a tall tree in the steppe. One Cossack climbed the tree to kept watch, while the other remained ready to ride back immediately upon sight of the enemy. The watchman, after climbing down, followed the Tatars to determine the direction of their movement. This work was very dangerous, because the Tatars hunted the sentries, both to prevent them from raising the alarm and to gain information about the current state of defenses. A surviving letter to the garrison commander at Novgorod-Seversky tells about the misadventures of one such lookout, Yakush, a Cossack from Putivl. In the fall of 1523, Yakush was ordered to guide a company of gentry servitors pursuing some Tatars escaping with loot and captives after a raid. The Russian detachment caught up with the Tatars and succeeded in freeing the captives. Yakush then guided everybody back to the frontier, after which he returned to his lookout station on the steppe. Unfortunately, the Tatars, annoyed at having to return empty-handed, decided to go back and search the area where the Cossacks kept watch. They caught Yakush and carried him away to the khan in Crimea. The subsequent fate of Yakush is unknown, but this little bit of recorded history gives us a glimpse of the everyday life on the edge, with its constant threat of the Tatar raids, the “posses” organized to pursue the robbers, and the precarious existence of the Cossacks serving as the frontier lookouts and guides.
```

```markdown
# 第一章

在第一章中我問道，一個國家，俄羅斯，是如何從受害者轉變為帝國的？ 一種答案的輪廓開始浮出水面。 從巡邏草原的科薩克人到邊境上的農民，再到莫斯科的博伊雅人，整個俄羅斯人民 instinctively 知道他們必須團結起來對抗來自遊牧民族的威脅。 這不是理性的計算，而是源於數百年文化變遷的結果，這種變遷出現在文明交匯線上的人生中。 Ведь всё могло быть так же в 1237 году, когда надвигалась неминуемая монгольская угроза. 在 1223 年與兩位成吉思汗將軍傑布和蘇博泰率領的遠征隊在卡爾卡戰役中消滅了俄羅斯-庫曼聯軍。 1236 年摧毀波羅茨克布爾加人的事件表明蒙古人計劃進行系統性的征服；然而，俄羅斯並沒有團結起來。 極具諷刺意味的是，每一個公國，如果取而代之，都表現出完全理性的行為。 每位公爵都在等待其他公爵團結起來並擊敗蒙古人。 因為每位公爵只控制著一支小軍隊，他的貢獻對共同的成功來說並不重要。 另一方面，他的潛在成本卻可能非常巨大（例如，他可能會被殺死）。 (例如，他可能會被殺死。) 不幸的是，相同的邏輯也支配了所有公爵的行為，導致沒有任何集體努力嘗試反擊拔都軍隊。 這種以個人理性為基礎但 collectively foolish 的反應對社會學家和經濟學家來說非常著名；它被稱為“公共領域悲劇”。

長時間的邊境條件導致俄羅斯文化發生了深刻的變化。 負責這種變化的一般社會機制稍後會討論； 現在，我只想確立文化變遷的事實。 與他們的先祖不同，莫斯科時期的人們表現出 collective astute 的方式，即使這樣做會給個人帶來困難或更糟。 如前所述，對共同善的solidarity 和犧牲意願並非基於理性的計算；它們有著 гораздо более глубокие foundations. 邊境邏輯“我們與他們”塑造了將世界劃分為善惡兩方面的觀點。 一側是基督教社區，代表著世界上的一切美好事物；另一側是魔鬼騎兵，崇拜他們的邪神並對基督徒犯下無法言喻的暴行。 這個黑白色的衝突觀點在第一章中引用的斯托格諾夫年代記摘錄以及十九世紀俄羅斯藝術家瓦西里·蘇里科夫創作的《埃馬克征服西伯利亞》這幅畫中都得到了 wonderfully captured. (請注意，我詳細說明了俄羅斯如何看待情況；突厥人自然有自己的 distinct 的觀點。)
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

宗教是將莫斯科社會緊密結合在一起的粘合劑。例如，人們願意“為信仰而受苦”——即為了做正確的事情，犧牲舒適和甚至生命本身，忍受艱難困境——這在人民中根深蒂固。雖然帶有信仰啟發的行為沒有明顯的社區生存功能，但它們間接總是對此做出貢獻。讓我們重新回到斯托格拉諾夫紀年錄，它描述了在關鍵戰役之前，阿塔曼們如何勸說科薩克人“為真正的正教信仰而受苦”。在與異教徒作戰中犧牲生命是一種虔誠行為。莫斯科人之所以合作，並非因為這是理性的做法，而是因為這是正確的做法。

利他合作並不是促使伊馬克的科薩克人與突厥人交戰的唯一動機。事實上，他們還有各種各樣的動機，其中希望獲得掠奪品當然不容忽視。總體而言，人們的行為受到自私利益、害怕懲罰和規範（社會決定的行為規則）的結合影響。大多數時候，人們以自我為中心地行事，但有時他們會做一些事情，不僅為了獲得物質獎勵或避免懲罰，僅僅因為這是正確的做法。做正確的事情的回報是非物質性的——例如內在滿足感和可能的社會認可。

現在考慮兩支體量相近的軍隊。這兩支軍隊中的士兵都得到相同的報酬，並且受到相同程度的懲罰，以處罰職責不履行。然而，在第一支軍隊中，士兵們僅僅由這些物質誘因來驅動，而第二支軍隊中的士兵則相信與敵人作戰是正確的做法。例如，他們可能會為了自己的信仰和國家而戰，或者他們認為自己人生的目標是對邪惡敵人的滅絕。當這兩支軍隊在戰場上交鋒時會發生什麼？除非發生奇蹟，否則第一支軍隊將瓦解並會被第二支軍隊擊敗。通常，在兩個群體之間的鬥爭中，擁有更強大的促進合作規範和更多人遵循這些規範的團體更有可能獲勝。
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

為了回到莫斯科邊境，我並非建議其防禦者完全僅僅受到非物質報酬的驅動。相反地，在俄羅斯邊境的僕人會收到現金、糧食和土地作為回報。未能服侍的人會受到懲罰。例如，如果任何人離開瞭望哨，而且沒有因為塔塔르突破而導致情況發生變化，他就會被鞭打。如果塔塔爾攻破了防禦線，這位疏忽的瞭望哨就會被處決。儘管獎勵和懲罰刺激確實存在，但莫斯科邊境的人民的動機不能僅僅歸結於這些純粹的物質誘因。他們也被激勵為了統治者和祖國，以及最重要的是信仰而戰鬥。

如同所有複雜的農業文明，莫斯科社會是按照等級制度組織起來的。從國家角度來看，存在兩種主要的人群：繳納稅款的人（農民和平民）和提供軍事服務的人。服務類別包括為莫斯科軍隊提供騎兵的世襲地主，以及火槍手、炮兵人員和團結人的非世襲服務階層。在十六世紀和十七世紀，莫斯科的核心地區發展出了一定的社會經濟不平等現象。大土地所有者佔據了社會頂端，奴隸和平民則充塞著底層。
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

The frontier，與此形成對比的是，具有更為平坦的社會階層結構，因為它缺乏金字塔頂端和底端。在邊疆北部地區僅存在大型莊園，而且數量遠少於居住在防禦線附近的 petty servicemen（小兵）。邊疆地區長期飽受人口短缺之苦，因此土地充裕。沒有無地農民，任何人都可以耕種所需的土地。稀少的居民也意味著軍事指揮官在徵召足夠守備邊疆的士兵方面面臨重重困難。徵召士兵的需求如此之急，以至於他們願意招募來自任何社會背景的人。隨著時間推移，從繳稅農民的行列轉移到世襲 servicemen（軍人）的行列。大多數 servicemen自己耕種土地，並且只有極少數有大量的農民。中央政府不喜歡邊疆有這麼少的農民和這麼多的 servicemen，因為這意味著收稅減少，但維持對圖們人的防禦至關重要。在 1640 年代，當局沒收了邊疆內的貴族擁有的土地，解放了農民，並將他們招募到騎兵營中服役。新的 servicemen 在從前主人的土地上獲得支持。同時，政府也邀請來自中央地區的所有貧困 servicemen 向南遷移，並給予他們土地和編入邊疆防禦力量。

這種不尋常的社會組成結構，由負有軍事服務義務的小地主所主導，是促進邊疆地區合作精神的另一項重要因素。等級和財富上的巨大差異會導致分裂。平等的人更容易達成共同的目的並制定共同行動方案。平等主義促進了合作。

再次指出，一些讀者，尤其是那些閱讀過關於俄羅斯歷史書籍的讀者，可能會問我是否在描繪俄羅斯邊疆社會的過於理想化的畫面。歷史書並沒有告訴我們莫斯科（Muscovy）是一個“東方專制統治”嗎？農民受到嚴厲壓迫嗎？甚至貴族也沒有權利，並且可以被用皮鞭（knout）或甚至是皇子的隨意命令處以死刑？在這樣的社會中，談論合作，尤其是平等主義，真的可能嗎？
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

Perceptions of historical processes are often affected by our cultural and ideological biases, and Russian history is one illustration of this. Much of what we know about early modern Russia came to us transmitted through the eyes of western Europeans, such as the envoy from the Austrian Empire, Sigismund von Herberstein, mentioned previously. These individuals were not trained anthropologists, and when we read their descriptions we must consider their various cultural preconceptions. For example, western European visitors made disapproving comments about the weird habit of the Russians to wash every week, on Sunday, even in winter. (Everybody knows that bathing is bad for your health!) Westerners also complained that Russians were not gentlemen. When insulted, instead of challenging to a duel, they sue in court! (This, unfortunately changed with time, and the dueling epidemic of the nineteenth century was to claim thousands of Russian noblemen’s lives, among them two of the language’s best poets, Pushkin and Lermontov.)

Russian history continued to suffer from observer biases even during the twentieth century. During the Cold War era, American writers often invoked the inherent predisposition of the Russians to autocratic rule to explain Stalin-era totalitarianism. Surprisingly, the Soviet historians concurred, although for a diametrically opposed reason. They contrasted the tsarist oppression with the workers paradise constructed by the Communists after the revolution. Only since the mid-1980s, and especially after 1990 and the end of the Cold War, have the archives become freely accessible to both Russian and Western historians, such that we have started to witness a new and much more impartial scholarship. In the “Notes and Further Readings” at the end of the book, I list several of these works.

Peasants were certainly oppressed in Russia, as in any other premodern state, including western European countries. However, the degree of oppression of the lower classes varied in space and with time. I have already pointed out that the frontier society was much more egalitarian than the central regions of Russia. In the central regions, however, the overall quality of the relations between lords and peasants changed quite dramatically from the fifteenth to the eighteenth century.
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

Enserfment 是一種在俄羅斯發展相對較晚的現象。 在十七世紀上半葉，農民離開地主的權利逐漸被剝奪。 這個過程 culminated 在 1649 年的法律編纂法 (Law Code of 1649)，這構建了束役制度的法律框架。 農民的經濟壓迫逐漸加劇，並在十八世紀末達到高峰。 因此， fifteenth 世紀自由農民與 eighteenth 世紀帝俄羅斯未免農奴之間存在著巨大的差異，後者像牲畜一樣可以被房主出售。 然而，我不應讓讀者產生地緣位置是唯一決定下層階級承受壓迫程度的因素的印象。 情況遠比這複雜得多，我將在第二部分“帝國病理學”(Imperiopathosis) 中進一步探討這個問題，我們將看到任何特定社會的不平等和壓迫程度是一種具有波動性的變量，並且會以數百年為週期來漲跌。

最後，重要的是要指出，合作並非總是“甜蜜與光明”。 人類既有驚人的自我犧牲精神，也有令人震驚的自私行為。 因此，在現實社會中的合作不能僅僅基於“ Kumbayah 精神”(政治科學家羅伯特·普諾姆 (Robert Putnam) 的話語)，而且必須包括像社區治安和懲罰這樣的令人不快的事情。 我之前提到，如果一名看守離開了職位，他將受到鞭打或處以死刑，具體取決於他的疏忽造成的後果。 在俄羅斯，人類的生命價值就像其他封建社會中的任何人的生命一樣廉價，因此，像刺穿 (impaling) 這樣的酷刑和殘忍而羞辱性的懲罰十分普遍。 儘管在克里米亞與莫斯科之間長期的鬥爭中，大多數暴行是由圖們恰人對俄羅斯人所犯的，這很大程度上歸因於機會的不平衡。 一旦領土被併入，任何反對中央政府的叛亂都會受到嚴厲鎮壓。 合作與殘酷之間不存在內在矛盾。 實際上，大規模的暴力行為，例如大屠殺，可以在封建社會中甚至在現代時期僅僅通過內部凝聚的團體來實現。 例如，可以思考納粹組織對猶太人、吉普賽人和塞爾維亞人的精確時間控制下的種族滅絕，其精度令人印象深刻。
```

```markdown
I HAVE ATTEMPTED TO SHOW THAT the dominant factor in the development of the Muscovite society was the frontier. The pressure from the steppe nomads molded Muscovy’s institutions and culture. I propose that a causal connection exists between the frontier position of Muscovy and its transformation into a strongly centralizing state, in which different social classes cooperated in territorial defense and expansion. This is a hypothesis, because a well-developed theory cannot be based on a single case, but let us continue the exploration of this idea for a while yet, before a more comprehensive test is taken.

So far my focus has been on cooperation at the local level. Cossacks, gentry servitors, peasants, and government officials worked together to defend a particular segment of the steppe frontier. Incidentally, given this social background, it is easier to see why Ermak’s Cossacks were able to withstand the Tatar onslaught at the battle of Sibir without breaking down. However, our ultimate goal is to understand how large territorial empires can be assembled and held together. Certainly, coercion from the center is one aspect of the answer. But, again, willing cooperation between the peripheries and the center makes it much easier for an empire to extend its sway. It is a mistake to think that empires are based solely on force—the largest ones always involved some degree of cooperation (and when cooperation declined, the empires crumbled). The Russian Empire was not an exception.

Whereas the forest-steppe fault line in eastern Europe divided the nomads and the farmers from each other, it integrated people located on the same side of the frontier. Farming people inhabiting the territory of the former Kievan Russia spoke very similar eastern Slavic languages (dialects, really) and belonged to the same branch of Christianity. Small cultural differences resulting from slight dialectal dissimilarities were dwarfed by the presence of the very different “other” on the other side of the frontier: Turkic, nomadic, Muslim. Cooperation is much easier to achieve among culturally similar people with similar goals, values, and behaviors.
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

In fact, conquest played a less-important role in Moscow’s expansion within the eastern Slavic lands than such nonviolent measures as dynastic inheritance, purchase, and even the patent from the khan of the Golden Horde. Of particular interest are the occasions when rulers of various principalities voluntarily entered the Moscow service. For example, in 1500, the princes of Novgorod-Severski, Chernigov, and Starodub deserted Lithuania and joined their lands to Muscovy. It is noteworthy that all of these principalities lie to the southwest of Moscow, right along the steppe frontier. By contrast, the strongest resistance to the expanding Muscovite power came from the principality of Tver and the free city of Novgorod the Great, which lie to Moscow’s northwest and were not as exposed to the Tatar raids. Both Novgorod and Tver were subdued by Moscow only after a long armed struggle.

History repeated itself in 1654 with the defection of Ukraine from Poland-Lithuania to Russia. When Poland and Lithuania merged in 1569, its aristocracy rapidly assimilated to the Polish language and Catholic religion, causing unrest among the Orthodox peasantry inhabiting the formerly Lithuanian lands (what is now Ukraine and Belarus). Resistance against the Polish authorities was spearheaded by the Dnieper Cossacks. These Ukrainian Cossacks established their headquarters, called the Sech, on an island below the Dnieper cataracts. They made a living very much like their Russian counterparts, alternating between service to the Polish state and raids against the Crimean Tatars and Turkey. The Sech Cossacks organized themselves as a military democracy, in which officials were elected, and all the important decisions were made at a gathering of all the Cossacks. This is yet another example of the tendency to egalitarianism on the frontier.

In the early seventeenth century, the pressure to convert to Catholicism intensified, while the Polish landlords imposed harsh economic oppression on Ukrainian peasants. Beginning in 1624, a series of peasant rebellions led by the Cossacks swept Ukraine. The Poles kept putting these revolts down, but with great difficulty. Finally, in 1653, the Ukrainians sent representatives to Moscow to ask to be taken under the tsar’s protection. The Muscovite government at first hesitated, because accepting this proposal would entail a war with Poland, for which Russia was not ready, but eventually the decision was made. The final step for the union was taken at a rada, or “general assembly,” in Pereiaslavl in 1654. The delegates to the rada debated at length their course of action. Previous struggle against Poland made clear to the Ukrainians that they were not strong enough to establish an independent state, so their only options were to submit to Poland or to transfer allegiance to either Turkey or Russia. The decisive factor in the final decision was the religious compatibility, and the Ukrainian assembly voted to submit to the Orthodox tsar.
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

TO AN AMERICAN, THE WORDS FRONTIER and frontiersman immediately conjure the visions of the Wild West, the Indians, the cowboys ... But are there any parallels between the American and Russian frontiers? What was the impact of the frontier on the European settlers who made their little homes on the American prairie?

The first European settlers to America arrived in Jamestown, Virginia, in 1607, followed shortly by the Dutch on Manhattan Island and the Pilgrims at Cape Cod. The frontier was a true fault line, on which two very different civilizations came in contact, soon to become conflict. On one side were the European farmers originating from urbanized literate societies with a monotheistic religion (mostly, assorted Protestant sects of Christianity). The various Indian societies, on the other side of the fault line, were almost a perfect opposite, except some Indians also practiced farming. Given such deep cultural differences, it was inevitable that the two groups of people would come into conflict. Indeed, the first war between the settlers and the Indians broke out in 1622, and the cross-fault line hostilities went on with few interruptions until the western frontier was officially declared closed in 1890. The conflict, therefore, was almost three centuries in duration.

Modern histories do not emphasize this aspect of the conflict, but it was very intense, at times genocidal. The history of the massacres that the U.S. Army inflicted on the Indians during the last 30 years of the conflict was powerfully told in 1970 by Dee Brown in *Bury My Heart at Wounded Knee*. However, both the Indians and Europeans committed genocide and atrocities. The Indians were more inventive in coming up with horrible tortures, but the settlers were ultimately more successful at exterminating the Indians.

We also tend to forget that the Indian Wars inflicted higher casualties in proportional terms than any other wars in American history. On the very first day of the first Indian War, between the Virginian settlers and the Powhattan Confederacy in 1622, the Indians massacred 347 men, women, and children out of the population of only 1,200. This is a casualty rate of 30 percent! By contrast, the American losses in the World Wars I and II were only 0.1 and 0.3 percent of the total U.S. population, respectively. In the Second Powhattan War, the Indians killed 500 out of 8,000 settlers. In the King Philip’s War of 1675-76, about 800 Puritans were killed out of the total population of 52,000. More than half of New England’s 90 towns suffered from Indian attacks. As Nathaniel Saltonstall wrote in 1676, “in Narranganset not one House [was] left standing. At Warwick, but one. At Providence, not above three.” It took years for the area to recover.
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

The violent acts committed by the Indians on the Whites were not limited to indiscriminant killing and property damage. During the King Philip’s War, the Indian atrocities included “the raping and scalping of women, the cutting off of fingers and feet of men, the skinning of White captives, the ripping open the bellies of pregnant women, the cutting off of penises of the males,” and so on. In 1675, the Wampanoag Indians raided the town of Lancaster, Massachusetts, where they killed 12 and captured 24 of its inhabitants. One of the captives, Mary Rowlandson, was the wife of a minister and later wrote a book about her experiences. During the raid, the Indians set her house on fire, forcing its occupants to leave even this inadequate shelter: “No sooner were we out of the house, but my brother-in-law (being before wounded, in defending the house, in or near the throat) fell down dead; whereat the Indians scornfully shouted, halloed, and were presently upon him, stripping his clothes. The bullets flying thick, one went through my side, and the same (as would seem) through the bowels and hand of my dear child in my arms. One of my elder sister’s children, named William, had then his leg broken, which the Indians perceiving, they knocked him on the head [that is, killed him]. Thus were we butchered by those merciless heathens, standing amazed, with the blood running down to our heels.” During the raid, Rowlandson’s baby, sister, brother-in-law, and nephew were killed, and another child died during the forced march after the attack. She was sold by her captors into slavery to another Indian, but eventually was ransomed out, after spending three months in captivity. Her book, published in 1682, became a bestseller.

One characteristic of the Indian warfare that was particularly repellent to the Whites was the torture of captives. Here’s one account of Shawnee torture published by Benjamin Franklin in the Pennsylvania Gazette in 1729: “They made the Prisoner Sing and Dance for some Time, while six Gun Barrels were heating red hot in the Fire; after which they began to burn the Soals of the poor Wretches Feet until the Bones appeared, and they continued burning him by slow Degrees up to his Privites, where they took much Pains ... This Barbarity they continued about six Hours, and then, notwithstanding his Feet were in such a Condition, they drove him to a Stake ... and stuck Splinters of Pine all over his Body, and put fire to them ... In the next Place they scalp’d him and threw hot Embers on his Head ... At last they ran two Gun Barrels, one after the other, red hot up his Fundament, upon which [he] expired.”
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

The settlers themselves were certainly no shrinking violets, and often conducted themselves in a manner as merciless as that shown by their adversaries。During the Powhattan War，Governor Wyatt invited several hundred Indians to a peace conference，where he attempted to poison them all。約 200 人變得劇烈地生病並被弗吉尼亞人屠殺，其他人（包括印第安領袖）逃脫。在菲利普王之戰期間，清教徒對非戰鬥人員進行了大規模屠殺。當他們俘虜了印第安勢力的領導人菲利普的妻子和九歲的兒子時，他們將她和眾多其他囚犯賣為奴隸。荷蘭人也 perpetrated  gerçekleştir 了他們的暴行之一。1643 年，荷蘭士兵襲擊了位於現今艾比尼基附近的一座瓦皮寧格印第安村莊。該村莊已經遭受莫哈克人的襲擊，殺害並奴役了許多男性，但卻保全了婦女和兒童。荷蘭人屠殺了所有倖存者，包括婦女和兒童。他們帶著 80 個印第安人的斷頭回到了紐阿姆斯特丹，用於在鎮上街道上進行一場恐怖的足球比賽。此外，還有 30 名囚犯被處以酷刑致死，以供公眾娛樂。

這些只是許多故事中的一部分，說明了北美洲印度人與定居者之間非凡的衝突強度。最近的一份彙編統計了白人對印第安人、印第安人對白人以及印第安人對其他印第安人犯下的超過 16,000 起記錄的暴行，在 268 年的衝突期間。這相當於每週超過一個暴行！實際上，還有很多更多，因為並非每次事件都會留下歷史記錄。當這些事件在報紙（如本傑明·富蘭克林報紙中描述的酷刑故事）和書籍（如瑪麗·羅蘭森暢銷書中所述）中報導時，對定居者社區的影響將遠大於在沒有文字的情況下。對於定居者人口的集體心理來說，持續收到這種報告的轟擊可能會產生巨大的心理衝擊。想像一下，如果 CNN 告訴你昨天又一個美國小鎮被“紅人”摧毀了。（讓我們不指定敵人的確切身份。）所有男性都被殺害、婦女被強姦並被殺死，那些沒有立即被屠殺的孩子則被帶走以在器官黑市上販賣。或者，“紅人”再次將一名美國士兵 torture 致死，錄製並重複播放在 Al Reddiyyah 頻道上。或者也許與一名被解救的囚犯的採訪關於她受“紅人”之手侵害的恐怖經歷。你會聽到這種故事每周一次，一輩子都在聽；而且當你的父母和祖父母長大時，情況也是一樣的。毫無疑問，任何承受著這種壓力幾代人的社會都會發生轉變。
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

One consequence of the life on the North American fault line was the famous American melting pot. Indeed, when confronted with such obvious aliens as painted, bloodthirsty, heathen redskins, two European settlers, even if they came from different countries, could not help but feel that they were kin. Thus, in the old Europe, although the Irish hated the English, and the French fought against the Germans, in the New World all these people cooperated with each other and fought together against the Indians. As a result of the shared feeling that they belonged together, they and their descendants rapidly assimilated to a common American culture and language. Note also the limits of the melting pot. Because the fault line was defined in racial terms, immigrants belonging to non-White races, such as the Negroes and the Chinese, were not accepted as the “Americans.” (This pattern began to change in the twentieth century.)

Another characteristic of the Americans, which was commented upon at length by that astute Frenchman Alexis de Tocqueville, was their exceptional ability to form voluntary associations. “Americans of all ages, all stations in life, and all types of disposition are forever forming associations. There are not only commercial and industrial associations in which all take part, but others of a thousand different types—religious, moral, serious, futile, very general and very limited, immensely large and very minute.” As a result of this proclivity to associate, the Americans could rapidly and effectively organize concerted collective action. “If some obstacle blocks the public road halting the circulation of traffic, the neighbors at once form a deliberative body; this improvised assembly produces an executive authority which remedies the trouble ... Public security, trade and industry, and morals and religion all provide the aims for associations in the United States. There is no end which the human will despairs of attaining by the free action of the collective power of individuals.” Or: “As soon as several Americans have conceived a sentiment or an idea that they want to produce before the world, they seek each other out, and when found, they unite. Thenceforth they are no longer isolated individuals, but a power conspicuous from the distance whose actions serve as an example; when it speaks, men listen.”
```

```markdown
FROM THE MONGOLS IN THE THIRTEENTH CENTURY, to the Muscovites in the sixteenth and seventeenth centuries, and then on to the Americans in the seventeenth through nineteenth centuries, we have romped through time and space. It is surprising how many things these societies have in common. The first and most obvious one is that they all were empire builders. It would not be an exaggeration to say that they built the three most powerful empires in world history. Less obviously, each of these three societies, although in its own culturally unique way, had a high capacity for concerted collective action. In fact, such a capacity seems to be a necessary condition for successful empire building. The society-level capacity for concerted action was, in turn, based on the ability of individuals to cooperate. Finally, all three peoples originated from intense and prolonged fault-line frontiers. (I have not yet presented the frontier origins of the Mongols, so for now you will have to take my word for it.)

Although each society achieved high capacity for concerted action, it is important to stress that specific cultural mechanisms employed to accomplish this were completely unique to each society. Fault-line frontiers have a strong influence on some aspects of societies, while leaving others indeterminate. Let us, for example, compare the Americans and the Muscovites. The basis for cooperation among the Americans was the voluntary civil association. The political organization of the Americans, accordingly, was democratic, and after they became independent of the British, they immediately set up a republic to govern their affairs. The ideological source of social power was solidly rooted in the popular will (the famous “we the people”). Whereas the Americans were deeply suspicious of the central government, the Muscovites, in contrast, embraced it as the fundamental organizing principle of their society. The form of government was a monarchy, or autocracy. The source of social power was not the people, but God’s will. Therefore, in theory, the tsar was not responsible to the common people for his actions, or even to the boyars. He answered for his deeds before God alone (at least this was how power was legitimated in Muscovy; in practice, of course, no ruler can last long if he does not take into account the wishes of his subjects).

It is natural for us to think that the American way is “good” and the Muscovite way is “bad.” Indeed, life is much more pleasant under a secular democracy than under an autocracy with strong theocratic elements. However, our ideological biases should not blind us to the basic fact that both societies, in their own ways, were extremely effective at solving the problems that they faced.
```

```markdown
Section path: Document

另一重要的差異在俄羅斯和美國社會之間，體現在他們區分“我們”與“他們”的主要方法上。通常，深層次的文化差異可以通過各種“標誌”來表現，包括語言或方言、宗教、外貌（種族、服裝、視覺符號或徽章）等方面的差異。然而，往往一個主導的指標能夠將兩批人民區分開來，位於對方的分界線上。在俄羅斯的情況下，這個指標是宗教，因此衝突主要在基督教正統派和穆斯林之間。俄羅斯紀年錄中對衝突的 religiously 充滿內容的語言是這一點的一個體現。因此，邊疆地區的整合作用僅適用於正統派團體。莫斯科人對波蘭立陶宛（烏克蘭人、白俄羅斯人）的正統派居民有強烈的親屬感，但對天主教徒（波蘭人）沒有這種感覺。實際上，正統派烏戈爾族對莫斯科人來說比天主教斯拉夫民族更為“我們”。一個有趣的推論是，當使用宗教作為主要指標時，來自其他文明的人們可以加入莫斯科社會——通過轉換信仰。有許多各階層的圖們人在接受正統基督教後成為莫斯科人的“我們”。許多科薩克人 pochodziły z baptized 图們人，在十七世紀，莫斯科貴族中，約佔 17% 是圖們人或圖們人的後裔。

美國社會通過種族標誌來區分自己與印第安人，無論印度教徒還是異教徒，他們仍然是外人。歐洲人和印第安人之間發生了相當數量的通婚，但跨越分界線通婚的個人經常會被排斥在外。對跨種族婚姻的抵觸情緒最強烈的是白 kadın 嫁給或與印度男性有性關係的女性。這種情況下，該女子將被排除在社區之外，並且在大多數情況下無法找到配偶，如果她單身了。邊疆地區的整合作用僅限於歐洲人血統的人們。在此時，有人可能會被誘惑到譴責種族主義的美國人和讚美更開放 minded 的莫斯科人，但這種價值判斷對我們理解帝國興衰沒有幫助。就本調查的目的而言，我們不會將歷史人物分類為“好人”與“壞人”。
```

Section path: Document

返回到本書的主要問題，我們發現了一個強大的宏觀歷史概括。 起源於邊境裂痕的人們變得具有合作性和高集體行動能力，從而使他們能夠建立大型且強大的領土國家。 換句話說，我們有了一個解釋帝國國家如何崛起為權力的理論的開端。 但這種將邊境裂痕與由此產生的強大國家聯繫起來的可能性是否只是巧合？畢竟，到目前為止我們只有三個例子。 下一個任務是找出所假設的關係是否普遍成立。 要做到這一點，我們前往萊茵河和多瑙河流域在公元一世紀前幾年期間的岸邊。

第 3 章

森林中的屠殺

在羅馬帝國的邊境

歐洲和地中海在公元一千年間是一個開始測試邊界理論的好地方，因為在該時期初期，這個地區完全由一個大型國家控制：羅馬帝國（參見圖 2）。 因此，我們只有一套相對穩定的帝國邊界可供考慮，這簡化了追蹤它們對後來繼任狀態發展的影響任務，尤其是在該千禧年後半葉。 如果先前章節中提出的概括證明是正確的，那麼居住在羅馬帝國後方的所有大型國家都應該是由起源於羅馬邊境的人們建立起來的。 我們預測，既不在舊帝國的核心地區居住，也不住在遠離邊境的非帝國“後方”地區居住的人們都不會成功地建立大型國家。

與羅馬帝國需要處理的各種邊界民族可以大致分為以下幾類：首先，有來自北歐森林的居民，主要是日耳曼人和（後來）斯拉夫人；其次，南部的邊境受到非洲和阿拉伯沙漠居民的威脅（柏柏爾人和阿拉伯人）；第三種情況是來自歐亞大陸草原的遊牧入侵者（匈奴人、阿瓦爾人等）；第四種情況是在羅馬帝國東部邊境的一種文明國家——波斯帝國（後來被薩珊波斯取代）。

![005](../image/turc_9781101126912_oeb_005_r1.gif)

圖 2

羅馬帝國及其繼承者：(a) 公元 300 年，(b) 公元 500 年，(c) 公元 800 年

羅馬帝國在傳統上於公元 476 年（西羅馬最後一位皇帝羅慕路斯·奧古斯都下台）崩潰後，在歐洲被多個國家所取代。 我們對大型領土國家感興趣，因此我只列出了那些在高峰期擁有超過大約 100,000 平方英里（0.3 百萬平方公里）的土地的羅馬繼任者。 要將這個閾值放在一個角度上，這相當於像意大利或波蘭這樣中型現代歐洲國家所擁有的土地面積。

```markdown
Section path: Document

Between 476 and 1000, Europe had seven large states: the empire of the Franks (reached the maximum area in A.D. 800 under the emperor Charlemagne), the kingdoms of the Ostrogoths (peak in 500) and the Visigoths (600), the khanates of the Avars (600) and the Bulgars (1000), the kingdom of Hungary (1000), and the Byzantine Empire (1000). In addition to the seven European states, two large states arose in the desert belt of North Africa and the Arabian Peninsula: the caliphate of the Arabs (750), and the Fatimid caliphate (960). Finally, three other states deserve mention: the kingdoms of Burgundians (600) and Langobards (600), whose size was smaller than the cut-off point of 100,000 square miles (and which were eventually annexed by the Frankish Empire), and the huge but very short-lived empire of the Huns (peak in 440), which collapsed soon after the death of its founder, Attila. In all of these cases, even the three borderline ones, frontier peoples established the empires: the Germans (Franks, Ostrogoths, Visigoths, Burgundians, and Langobards), the desert nomads (the Arabs and the Berbers), and the steppe nomads (Huns, Avars, Bulgars, and Magyars). In other words, the macrohistorical generalization proposed in Chapter 2 is splendidly confirmed. The only apparent exception is the Byzantines, but as we discuss later in this chapter, the Byzantine Empire in actuality fits the predictions of the theory quite well.

Let us now take a closer look at the ethnic groups that lived on the Roman frontier, and trace their fortunes after the Roman Empire collapsed. It is not enough to know that a strong correlation exists between location on the frontier and the rise of imperial nations; we also need to examine the specific techniques that these nations used in building empires, and what role (if any) cooperation played in this process. This chapter focuses on the northern frontier, running along the Rhine and Danube rivers; Chapter 4 covers the developments on the southern—desert—frontier.

THE ROMANS CALLED THEIR FRONTIERS *limites* (singular, *limes*). The Latin word *limes*, from which the English word “limit” is derived, originally meant a path between the fields, not a wall or an edge, as might be imagined. During the early empire, the frontiers were just that—frontier roads that made the movements of troops easy.
```
